    Complete Collections of Ancient and Modern Books, Medical Section, Volume 406

    Pediatric Internal Organs and Symptoms

    Direct Instructions for Children (Song Dynasty, Qian Yi)

    Five Organs: Deficiency and Excess, Cold and Heat

    The heart governs surprise. In cases of excess, the child cries and has a fever, and may twitch when drinking water; in cases of deficiency, the child feels weak and has palpitations. If there is excess heat in the heart, the child may sleep with their face up or grind their teeth; this is treated with Daohong San. If the heart qi is excessive and the child prefers to lie on their back, this is treated with Xiexin Tang.[1p]
    [Note: If there are signs of excess heat in the heart and small intestine, treat with previous medicines. If there is deficiency in the heart and spleen blood, use Wumei Yigong San combined with Angelica. If due to insufficient heart blood, use Mi Zhi An Shen Wan. For dryness of liver and heart blood, use Chai Hu Zhi Zi San. If there is deficiency of liver and heart blood, use Liu Wei Di Huang Wan. If due to spleen deficiency causing food stagnation and phlegm leading to fright and unrest, use Si Jun Zi to strengthen the spleen, Shen Qu and Mai Ya to aid digestion, and Shan Zhi and Chai Hu to clear heat. If the above formulas are used and the illness persists, promptly adjust to replenish the vital energy; or if symptoms worsen, urgently warm and replenish the vital energy. This often results from pregnancy with rich flavors and emotional fluctuations, or from improper breastfeeding in infants, or from the nursing mother's diet and emotional disturbances. Once the illness manifests and vital energy is deficient, one must trace the causes and primarily support the stomach to strengthen energy, complemented by medicines to treat the disease. I will follow this approach.]

    The liver governs wind; if there is excess, the face will turn green, eyes will be straight, and there will be loud crying and strong heat with neck tightness and restlessness; if there is deficiency, there will be teeth grinding and yawning.

    When there is heat in the liver, the hands grasp at clothing and fidget with objects; use Xie Qing Wan for this. For intense heat, drinking water causes wheezing; use Xie Bai San for this.

    [Note: If there are symptoms of liver wood excess heat causing wind and self-illness, and if lung metal is in excess heat affecting wood, use the previous two medicines to dispel the excess evil qi.][2p]
    If there is wind-heat in the liver channel with symptoms like straightening of the eyes, use Chai Hu Zhi Zi San to clear liver fire, and add Wei Si Wu Tang to nourish liver blood. If there is kidney deficiency with symptoms like teeth grinding, use Liu Jun Zi Tang to strengthen the spleen, and Liu Wei Di Huang Wan to nourish kidney water. If one does not carefully examine the signs of deficiency or excess and improperly uses the above medications, the dangers of deficiency will be unavoidable. Be cautious!

    If there is wind in the liver, the eyes are linked with disturbance; if there is heart heat, it leads to convulsions, or the tendons and veins are pulled leading to direct vision. Use Xie Qing Wan to treat the liver and Dao Chi San to clear the heart.

    If there is liver heat, the eyes are red, and if accompanied by convulsions, also use the above two medications. If the wind is severe, the body becomes stiff and tense; use Di Huang Wan to tonify the kidneys and Xie Qing Wan to treat the liver.

    Note: For the previous symptoms, if there is excess heat in the liver channel, Xie Qing Wan is appropriate. If the blood in the liver channel is dry and causes diseases, then Yi Gan San should be used. If kidney water is insufficient to nourish the liver, then Di Huang Wan is suitable. If the spleen soil is weak and cannot strengthen the wood, Liu Jun Zi Tang should be employed.

    In cases where the liver channel is already affected, the clash of wind and fire leads to damage to the spleen. If the fundamental is not secured, other symptoms will inevitably emerge.

    The spleen governs worries; if there is excess, the body heat leads to thirst, use Xie Huang San; if deficient, vomiting and diarrhea lead to wind, use Yi Gong San.

    Facial pallor, abdominal pain, cold qi in the mouth, loss of appetite, or vomiting clear water—use Yi Huang San for warming and supplementation. For spleen deficiency with diarrhea, use Tiao Zhong Wan.

    Frequent yawning and sleepiness indicate spleen qi deficiency that may provoke fright.[3p]
    According to previous evidence, if there is fever with thirst, a preference for cold food and drink, or diarrhea with yellow color, and the person sleeps with their eyes open, this indicates a condition of both heat and fullness in the body, and it is advisable to use the Xie Huang San to drain and guide it. If there is fever with dry mouth, aversion to cold food and drink, or diarrhea with white color, and the person sleeps with their eyes closed, this indicates a condition of both cold and deficiency in the body, and it is appropriate to use the Yi Gong San to adjust and tonify it. If the spleen qi is sinking, the Bu Zhong Yi Qi Tang should be used for elevation and tonification. If cold water insults the earth element, the Yi Huang San should be applied for warming and supplementation. If the liver wood overcomes the earth element, the Liu Jun Cha Hu Ping Bu should be used for balancing and tonifying. If there are slight eye movements, tidal heat, convulsions, vomiting, and diarrhea with loss of appetite, it is recommended to use the Mi Zhi Bao Pi Tang. For pediatric ailments, one should first regulate and tonify the spleen and stomach to solidify the foundation, leading to the resolution of all diseases.

    The lungs govern喘 (asthma), and if there is fullness, it leads to obstruction, turmoil, and rapid breathing with difficulty when drinking water; if there is deficiency, it results in a choking sensation and difficulty exhaling.

    If there is lung heat, one can use the Gan Ju Tang for treatment, which involves using the hands to touch the eyebrows, eyes, nose, and facial area.

    If lung excess is further affected by wind and cold, it leads to fullness in the chest, qi obstruction, wheezing, and distressing breaths. First, use the Xie Bai San to clear lung qi, followed by the Da Qing Gao to disperse wind and cold.

    If the lung organ is weak, resulting in pale lips, the Ejiao San should be employed to tonify. Conditions of obstruction, turmoil, coarse breathing, rapid shallow breaths, and choking sensations are difficult to treat, indicating severe lung deficiency.[4p]
    【Note: If the pores are not closed tightly and external pathogens affect the lungs, use Clear Lung Pills. If there is a deficiency of spleen and stomach qi, which cannot nourish the lungs, use Six Gentlemen Decoction. If there is excess spleen and stomach qi leading to constipation and lung disease, use Yellow Drainage Powder. If heart fire is scorching the lung metal, use Rehmannia Pills.】 The kidneys govern deficiency; if the fetal essence is weak and the spirit insufficient, with lackluster eyes and pale complexion, these are signs of difficulty in nurturing; even if one conceives, life will not be long. If desires further complicate the situation, many varied symptoms will arise, making recovery more challenging. If one is sensitive to light and feels a sinking sensation, it is due to heavy bones and a contracted body; if one grinds their teeth, it is because kidney fluid is insufficient to control heart fire; both should use Rehmannia Pills. 【Note: According to Mr. Jie Gu, the sinking sensation indicates insufficient kidney qi, resulting in heat in the lower limbs, hence the dislike of clothing covering them. Below the navel is governed by the kidneys, as heart qi descends to the kidney area, thus it is appropriate to use Rehmannia Pills to bolster water, control fire, and nourish the kidneys. Therefore, one must ensure that essence and blood are fully established before marriage, in order to avoid previous issues. The Essence and Blood section states: If a man's essence is not fully developed and he engages with a woman, to share his essence, then there will be deficiencies in various parts of the body, and there may be troublesome conditions. Now, if a child’s endowment is insufficient, isn’t this derived from the same cause?】[5p]
    The Treatment of Organ Interactions

    When liver disease appears in autumn, the liver is strong and overtakes the lungs, causing lung weakness. It is advisable to use Ejiao San to nourish the lungs, Yiyuang San to strengthen the spleen, and Xieqing Wan to treat the liver.

    [Note: According to Mr. Jie Gu Zhang, when the liver overpowers the lungs, the body feels hot, leading to spasms, shortness of breath, and symptoms appearing during the periods of Shen, You, and Xu. This is described as true strength, unable to conquer due to external constraints. If the heart takes control of the liver as a real pathogenic factor, there is strong heat and significant spasms. For this situation, Li Jing and Liang Jing Wan can be administered. When the lungs take control of the liver as a thief's evil, the patient experiences yawning and weak spasms. For this, Di Huang Wan is used to nourish the liver, while Xie Bai San is employed to treat the lungs.

    When the liver overcomes the spleen as a thief's evil, the patient feels sleepy, heavy in body, and experiences spasms, with Xieqing Wan being the treatment of choice. If the kidneys overcome the liver as a vacuous evil, the patient experiences a dislike of cold, yawning, and spasms; in this case, Qiang Huo Gao is indicated. Generally, in cases of liver disease, one must first examine the condition of the lungs and kidneys. The kidneys are the mother of the liver, and metal is the thief of wood; without kidney water, they cannot nourish each other, leading to the lung metal's spirit evil attacking. Therefore, when the source is in the lungs, one must first treat the lungs to dispel the spirit evil; if the source is in the kidneys, one should first nourish the kidneys to support their foundation. Then, one should assess the vacuity or repletion of the root organ and determine whether warming or cooling treatments are necessary. This approach aligns with the views of Liang Baoren as well.**[6p]
    Heart disease in winter manifests when the heart is stronger than the kidneys. In severe cases, there may be a descent causing lack of speech. One should use the Di Huang Wan to tonify the kidneys and Dao Chi San to treat the heart.

    Note: According to Jie Gu, if there is wheezing with strong heat, this indicates the lungs invading the heart, which is a slight evil, treated with Xie Bai San. If there is a clash of wind and heat, this indicates the liver invading the heart, representing a deficiency evil, treated with Da Qiang Huo Tang and Da Qing Wan. If there is vomiting and diarrhea with body heat, this indicates the spleen invading the heart, representing a solid evil, treated with Xie Huang San. If there is fear accompanied by chills, this indicates the kidneys invading the heart, representing a thief evil, treated with An Shen Wan.

    Generally, when there is heart disease, one must first regulate the liver. The kidneys are the spirit of the heart. When the liver’s qi is smooth, the heart’s qi is harmonious; when the liver’s qi is weak, the heart’s qi is deficient. Thus, for heart ailments, first address the liver to clear the source. When the five organs are ill, it must be transmitted to those they conquer; therefore, when the kidneys are afflicted, it will inevitably affect the heart. Hence, first treat the kidneys to expel the evil. If the liver and kidneys are balanced and there is still heart illness, then one should examine the deficiency and fullness for treatment.

    Lung disease manifests in spring when the lungs are stronger than the liver, treated with Xie Bai San for the lungs. If the eyes are pale blue or red, there may be convulsions, indicating liver deficiency, treated with Di Huang Wan to tonify the liver.

    Note: According to Jie Gu, if lung disease presents with wheezing and strong qi, appearing at the times of Yin, Mao, and Chen, one should tonify the liver and drain the lungs. If lung disease persists with cough, it is advisable to tonify the spleen and clear the heart. If the heart invades the lungs, representing a thief evil, with heat and wheezing, use Di Huang Wan, Dao Chi San, and E Jiao San.[7p]
    If the liver affects the lungs as a subtle pathogen, leading to symptoms like dizziness and confusion caused by evil wind, use Qianghuo Powder. If the kidneys affect the lungs as a solid pathogen, causing chills and a clear cough, use Baibu Pill. If the spleen affects the lungs as a vacuous pathogen, resulting in heaviness, phlegm, and diarrhea with cough, use Ginseng and Atractylodes Powder. Generally, when the lungs are ill, one must first examine the heart and spleen to treat them. If heart fire is excessive and burns the lungs, leading to lung disease, it is necessary to first suppress heart energy. If lung energy is insufficient and the pores are not tight, resulting in sensitivity to wind pathogens, it is essential to first bolster spleen energy. If there is fullness and stagnation in the middle jiao and heat vapor rises, one should first regulate spleen energy. If heart and spleen are balanced, then treat the primary channels.

    When kidney illness presents in summer, when water overwhelms fire, the kidneys affect the heart, which may lead to severe palpitations and spasms, and the remedy is to disperse the wind.

    (Note: According to Jiegugu, if the heart influences the kidneys, it is a subtle pathogen, causing fever without aversion to wind or cold; use Cinnamon Twig Pill. If the lungs influence the kidneys as a vacuous pathogen, causing wheezing and cold dampness on the skin, use Baibu Pill. If the liver affects the kidneys as a solid pathogen, causing rigidity and spasms with cold body symptoms, use Lihong Pill. If the spleen influences the kidneys as a thief pathogen, resulting in heaviness, diarrhea, and aversion to cold, use Lihong Pill. Generally, among the five elements, the kidneys are the only organ where the mother is strong and the offspring suffers from pathogens. However, the nature of things can’t be generalized, notably with the lungs and kidneys.)[8p]
    What does this mean? The lungs govern qi; if there is heat in the lungs, it generates heat and upward steam, preventing it from nourishing the kidneys, thus causing evil to affect the kidneys. Hence, the source of kidney disease lies in the lungs. Furthermore, dampness from the spleen channel can harm the kidneys; therefore, it is necessary to clear lung heat and remove spleen dampness. If the disease arises from this channel itself, it should be nourished and supplemented.

    Spleen diseases manifest nearby; they should be treated similarly. Those that present normally are easy to treat, while those that present abnormally are difficult to treat. If the spleen is deficient, the complexion will appear yellow. The five organs interact; treatment should follow the symptoms.

    Note: According to ancient texts, when diseases of the spleen arise, one must first examine the deficiency or excess of the liver and heart and treat accordingly. The liver is the spleen's thief, while the heart is the spleen's mother. If liver qi is strong, it hinders the spleen; if heart qi is deficient, the spleen becomes weak. Thus, when the liver overacts on the spleen, it leads to wind-dampness causing vomiting; in such cases, the method of administering Fu Ling and Ban Xia decoction is appropriate. If heart qi is robust and there is strong heat, leading to heaviness and diarrhea, one should resort to Qiang Huo, Huáng Qín, Cāng Zhú, and Gān Cǎo decoction. If the lungs overact on the spleen causing coughing and constipation while diet is normal, then Chefing and Dà Huáng decoction should be administered, along with the use of Téng Li Wán. If the kidneys overact on the spleen resulting in aversion to cold and diarrhea, methods like the Rì Zhōng Wán should be used.

    I humbly believe that the symptoms of the five organs interact in ways that are concealed and unpredictable, yet the mechanism of disease does not stray from the principles of the five elements of generation, overcoming, and transformation. Furthermore, since children do not have the seven emotions fully developed, their ailments often arise from weak and frail constitutions and incomplete blood and qi, leading to diseases where the five organs overpower each other. Therefore, one should prioritize treating the mother (root cause) rather than focusing solely on the child (symptoms), as this often leads to mistakes.[9p]
    Secret of Infant Care
    (Ming Dynasty, Wan Quan)

    General Discussion on the Diagnosis and Treatment of the Five Organs

    All diseases arise from the five organs; if one does not understand the organs and bowels, it is futile. By carefully combining color and pulse for diagnosis, it is not difficult to adapt prescriptions and treat ailments. When the five organs are in harmony, no disease arises. Whether it be due to imbalances from cold and heat or disruptions in diet, maladies arise: wind injures the liver, heat affects the heart, cold harms the lungs, dampness injures the kidneys, and dietary issues damage the spleen. Correspondingly, the colors are as follows: the liver is green, the heart red, the spleen yellow, the lungs white, and the kidneys black. For the pulses: the liver is string-like, the heart is surging, the spleen is slow, the lung is fine, and the kidneys are deep. In terms of symptoms, the liver governs wind, the heart is associated with fright, the spleen deals with fatigue, the lungs are linked to wheezing, and the kidneys signify deficiency. Regarding treatment: the heart, lungs, and spleen may have both tonifying and reducing methods, while the liver solely has reducing techniques, and the kidneys have only tonification without reduction. The assessment of color, pulse, symptoms, and treatment is fundamentally based on the five organs; understanding this deeply is termed superior skill. Among the five organs, the liver is often excessive, the spleen commonly insufficient, and the kidneys frequently deficient. The heart's heat equates it with fire, akin to the liver, while the delicate lungs, once injured, do not easily recover. People often say the liver is easily excessive and the spleen often deficient; I also say the heart is often excessive and the lungs often deficient. Excess indicates fullness, while deficiency indicates emptiness.[10p]
    The "Inner Canon" says: When pathogenic Qi is strong, there is fullness; when the true Qi is depleted, there is emptiness. This refers to what is in excess and what is insufficient, not merely the distinction between fullness and emptiness as stated in the classics. The liver, when in excess, belongs to wood, thriving in spring, which is the season of the lesser yang energy, the source for all things to flourish. The newborn is called a sprout because it is like the buds of grass and trees, which are initially nourished by the vital energy and are at their most vigorous stage; hence, it is said that the liver is in excess. Excess indicates a natural surplus of yang.

    The spleen is often deficient because it governs the energy of earth. In infancy, the only nourishment is breast milk; since solid food has not yet been ingested, the spleen has not yet been engaged in its function, and thus its energy remains weak. Therefore, it is said to be insufficient. Insufficiency indicates a natural deficiency of dietary energy.

    The heart is also described as having an excess; it belongs to fire and thrives in summer, which is the manifestation of vigorous fire energy. The kidney, however, signifies deficiency, as it refers to the lack of vital essence inherited from the parents after birth. The lungs too are often deficient; they are delicate organs, difficult to regulate and easily injured. Both the spleen and the lungs belong to the greater yin, and can be harmed by the extremes of cold and heat in nature; should one be affected, the lungs are the first to suffer; similarly, the cold and heat in food can harm the spleen first when in excess. Thus, it is said that both the spleen and the lungs are deficient.

    The liver is associated with wind and wood, governing the generation of wind, with manifest symptoms clearly observable in the eyes.[11p]
    Although purging is of no use to tonify, the energy of the lesser yang is akin to spring.

    The liver, associated with the foot Jueyin and the wood element, generates wind, and thus it governs wind. According to the Qian family, the liver governs wind; in fact, it manifests through the eyes with straight gazes, loud calls, yawning, irritability, and a tight neck. If deficient, there may be teeth grinding and excessive yawning; if heat is present, symptoms manifest externally, while damp qi arises internally. These are indications of liver disease. The liver’s orifice is the eyes, so when ill, one often observes symptoms through the eyes. If there is wind in the liver, the eyes may twitch; if there is heat, the gaze may be direct; if there is liver disease, conditions such as a white membrane covering the eyes may occur. Furthermore, the liver governs the tendons, and if diseased, the tendons may be tight, leading to a stiff neck and spasms. The liver governs anger; if afflicted, one may display a hasty temperament, loud cries, and severe cases may lead to testicular swelling, commonly referred to as "qi lump." When the liver is in the lower jiao, heat can cause difficulty in urination and bowel movements. The liver houses the soul; if liver heat is present, one may search for clothing, fidget with objects, or in severe cases, grasp at empty space and touch the bed, indicating a loss of soul.

    The Qian family notes a formula called "Xieqing Pill" for liver disease but does not suggest tonification, declaring that liver qi is excessive. However, the liver belongs to the lesser yang; thus, it is essential for nurturing life. A healthy liver should not be purged to diminish vital energy, nor should it be tonified to promote growth.

    The liver and gallbladder were originally treated with fire; within wood, there is fire that no one recognizes.[12p]
    Water cannot overcome the fire of the dragon thunder; only sweet and warm differences can control it. Diseases of the liver and gallbladder treated by fire stem from the existence of fire within wood. The "Records of the Fire Man" states: knowing that there is fire in the void, when wood is pleasing, it becomes bright. This is its verification. The fire of the liver and gallbladder cannot be extinguished by water or subdued by cold; it is also called the fire of the dragon thunder. Only sweet and warm remedies, such as ginseng and licorice, can control it. Therefore, it is said that sweetness can drain fire. The "Internal Classic" states: pungent substances disperse it, such as Chuanxiong and Fangfeng. It also states: pungent and sweet disperse for the yang. Using pungent and sweet medicines together, the so-called fire stagnation can be released. This is the general principle for treating liver diseases.

    For liver heat, one may drain it with Qingpian pills or Danggui and Aloe pills. For a firm liver, the same method applies. For liver deficiency, it is replenished with the Six-Flavor Rehmannia Pill. The liver is the child of the kidney; when deficient, one should nourish its mother. For liver cold, one uses the Wendan Decoction along with Wu Zhu Yu and ginger.

    In children’s diseases, if they cannot focus their gaze, or if their eyes do not move or cannot close, or if they open their eyes but cannot close them, or if they cry without tears, or do not cry but tears flow, all indicate a severe liver condition.

    The heart is the dwelling of the spirit, easily startled, with colors and pulses intertwined, suffering from the invasion of heat. In reality, one should avoid suspicion by draining the bowels. If there is deficiency and anxiety, one must calm the spirit.[13p]
    The "Inner Canon" states: The heart is the official of the sovereign, from which spirit and clarity emerge. At birth, a child’s awareness is not yet developed; their perception is easily stirred, hence their spirit is timid and prone to fright. Qian's perspective indicates: the heart governs fright. In actuality, this manifests as crying and fever, or restlessness after drinking water. In deficiency, there is fatigue, palpitations, and unease—this indicates a heart ailment. The heart governs blood vessels; color reflects the essence of blood, while pulse indicates the heart's condition. If the complexion appears rosy and the pulse is strong and frequent, it signifies an excess of heart qi, making the child easier to nurture. Conversely, if the complexion appears dull and the pulse is weak and fine, it indicates deficiency, leading to illness and making the child difficult to care for. Observing the shape, color, and pulse reveals the heart's true state. The heart dislikes heat; when it contends with wind, it leads to convulsions, hence the liver produces wind, which, when heated by the heart, results in convulsions. The heart is associated with fire; when fire is intense, body fluids become depleted, causing thirst. The heart houses the spirit; in heat, the spirit becomes chaotic, leading to restlessness in sleep. If a child prefers to sleep with their face covered, it indicates that heart qi is hot and the chest feels warm, making it hard to speak yet desiring coldness, thus they cover their face when sleeping. When heart qi is abundant, it moves freely; covering the face can obstruct qi flow, hence the preference for sleeping on the back. If the body is stretched upwards, this is termed "ascending," which also indicates heart heat. The tongue is the sprout of the heart.[14p]
    When overheated, the tongue becomes ulcerated, leading to conditions such as heavy and wooden tongue, and an elongated tongue that does not retract. The "Inner Canon" states that all pains, itching, sores, and ulcers relate to heart heat. Conditions in children such as tumors, red spots, rashes, and skin ailments are all attributed to heart heat.

    The Qian family treats heart heat diseases with Daohong San, which is a laxative for the small intestine. The heart is the sovereign and should not be disturbed; laxatives are used to avoid suspicion. If the heart is deficient, the ruler is uneasy, hence Anshen Wan is used to nourish it.

    The heart is the organ of fire; it often suffers from dispersion without consolidation. Master Sun's Shengmai San is to be taken in summer; its sourness from Schisandra can consolidate the dissipated energy. For treating children's heart conditions, one can expand and fill the heart. Therefore, for internal heart heat diseases, remedies like Daohong San, Xuanshen Decoction, and Dongyuan Anshen Wan are appropriate; for external manifestations like sores in the mouth or tongue, Xixin San is indicated. For those with deficient heart Qi, Qian's Anshen Wan is recommended; for those who easily startle, Hupo Baolong Wan is suitable. The "Inner Canon" states: to purge with bitterness, take Huanglian; to supplement with saltiness, take Zexie and Cheqianzi.[15p]
    Excessive spirit leads to more fright; it is advisable to use vermilion, red resin, and dragon bones to calm it. If the heart condition persists, sweating may emerge; the tongue may protrude and not retract, or a sudden loss of voice may occur, or confusion of the mind, or purplish rashes turning black. These all indicate a severed heart condition, which cannot be treated.

    In pediatric prescriptions, many spleen diseases arise simply from excessive dairy and food intake, leading to persistent ailments. Whether from hunger or fullness, both can create illness, as cold and heat invade, disrupting the qi.

    The "Inner Canon" states: the spleen and stomach are the officials of storage, where food and grains are gathered. At birth, the spleen is thin and weak, and can easily be harmed by food, hence it is said that the spleen is often insufficient. Qian says: the spleen governs heaviness; when it is full, there is tiredness and warmth followed by thirst; when it is deficient, it produces vomiting and diarrhea leading to wind. This indicates spleen disease.

    The spleen belongs to earth, which is stable, hence spleen diseases favor heaviness. Earth governs dampness. When dampness damages, it leads to swelling, bloating, jaundice, and persistent vomiting or diarrhea, resulting in chronic convulsions. The "Inner Canon" states: under the energy of earth, wood energy supports it. Earth represents the earth itself, and this relates to the abdomen; therefore, spleen diseases may manifest as abdominal pain, and spleen-related conditions result in a distended abdomen and blue veins.

    The orifice of the spleen is the lips; if there is wind in the spleen, the mouth may twitch and the lips move; if there is heat, there may be bad breath and sores on the lips; if there is cold, drooling at the corners of the mouth occurs, known as stagnation of the lips. When the qi is not harmonized, the mouth may frequently pucker.[16p]
    The spleen governs the tongue; when there is heat, it causes the tongue to be thrust out and moved about. The spleen governs flesh; when the spleen is deficient, one becomes thin, and the flesh breaks down. The spleen governs taste; when the spleen is deficient, one lacks appetite, while excess heat in the spleen means that food does not produce muscle tissue. Injury from food may lead to accumulation, and prolonged accumulation can result in habitual disorders. The spleen governs body fluids; heat in the spleen causes dry mouth and a need for water. In deficiency, body fluids do not generate, leading to sores.

    Regarding the differences and similarities between the spleen and stomach, it is said that the stomach receives grains, while the spleen transforms them. To regulate the spleen and stomach, one must adapt to their respective cold and warmth and manage their diet. Therefore, overeating damages the stomach, while hunger harms the spleen; heat injures the stomach, while cold affects the spleen.

    The stomach prefers coolness, while the spleen enjoys warmth; thus, one cannot treat them the same. Yin and yang must harmonize for balance, and one must not rely solely on either extreme of heat or cold.

    The spleen prefers warmth and dislikes cold, while the stomach enjoys coolness and shuns heat; their preferences differ, making it difficult to adhere to a single method. The spleen and stomach belong to the earth element, located centrally to respond to their surroundings. Hence, the principles must include the four seasonal qi and the harmony of the five tastes. The four qi are cold, heat, warmth, and coolness. The five tastes are sour, bitter, sweet, pungent, and salty. Pungent and sweet represent yang, while sour, bitter, and salty represent yin. When qi and taste combine, it is termed yin-yang harmonization, achieving balance. An excess of heat damages the stomach, while an excess of cold harms the spleen; this is not the middle path.[17p]
    The Qian family's method of treating conditions is to use Yi Huang San to nourish the spleen. The Elder Dongyuan stated that this method is too heating, and he replaced it with Yi Gong San, demonstrating deep consideration. The ancestral teaching emphasizes that the various methods of the Qian family should be followed. However, regarding the stomach and spleen, for spleen heat, use Xie Huang San; for stomach heat, use Ren Shen Bai Hu Tang; for cold in the spleen and stomach, use Li Zhong Tang Wan; for deficiency of the spleen and stomach, employ Yi Gong San, Tiao Yuan Tang, Ren Shen Bai Shu San, and Yang Pi Wan; for food stagnation, use Xiao Ji Wan and Bao He Wan; for lingering food accumulation, use Zhi Po Da Huang Wan; for dampness prevailing, use Wei Ling Wan; for evolving sores, use Fei Er Wan; and for already formed sores, use Ji Sheng Wan. This is a secret method of our family and should not be disclosed lightly.

    If the disease of the spleen persists for a long time, there may be noticeable weight loss, swollen abdomen, visible blue veins, inability to open the mouth, or the mouth and lips may be excessively opened, or there could be generalized swelling, swelling of the tops of the feet, swelling under the eyes, or incessant vomiting and diarrhea with an inability to take in food. Sleep may be disturbed with the eyes remaining open and the mouth not closing, or there may be excessive eating with weight loss, a craving for sweets, or worms emerging from the mouth, or the lips may be pulled tight - all these signs indicate a severe state of the spleen and are untreatable.

    The lung is a delicate organ and the primary source of qi; both cold and heat can invade and cause its qi to rebel.[18p]
    Heat clogs the chest, causing high panting and unrest; weakness and shortness of breath make it hard to return to tranquility. The lungs are the most elevated, serving as the crown of the organs. The mouth and nose are interconnected, and the inhalation and exhalation of breath, as well as the rise and fall of energy, must pass through them, thus they govern breath. According to the Qian family, the lungs control panting, which indeed manifests as disordered and rapid breathing; some may drink water, while others may not; if deficient, there’s prolonged difficulty in exhaling. This is a symptom of lung disease. The Nanjing states: cold harms the lungs. If a child wears clothing that is too thin, it may lead to cold injury. The Neijing states: heat harms the lungs. If a child is overdressed, it may lead to heat injury. Cold and heat injury the lungs causes reversed qi, resulting in panting and coughing. The nose is the orifice of the lungs; if the lungs are affected by wind, sneezing and a runny nose occur; if affected by cold, it results in nasal congestion and difficult breathing; if affected by heat, it causes dryness of the nose, or even nosebleeds; lung sores lead to red and ulcerated nostrils. The lungs govern the skin and hair; if the lungs are deficient, the skin becomes dry and the hair scorched. In cases of persistent panting and coughing, if panting does not stop, the face becomes swollen; if coughing does not stop, the sternum becomes protruded, referred to as "turtle chest." Sudden shock leads to a sign of death. The lungs belong to metal, and their essence is dry; in illness, there is unquenchable thirst and a preference for drinking water, known as "diaphragmatic consumption." The true diaphragm and lung qi communicate with heaven; medicinal use of clear soup is analogous to this. When the lungs are full, ephedra vigorously drains white, while donkey-hide gelatin provides extraordinary benefit for deficiency.[19p]
    The "Inner Canon" states: The weather connects to the lungs, light and clear represent the sky, and clear yang emerges from the upper orifices; what comes from the heavens is closest to the top. Therefore, for treating lung diseases, one should use pungent and sweet medicines that promote elevation and dispersion. If it's bitter and sour, it must be stir-fried with alcohol to encourage ascent. According to Qian's established prescriptions, for excess lung conditions, one should use Xie Bai San or Ting Li Wan; for deficiency, use Ejiao San. The ancestral teachings say the method is too simple. The lungs govern panting and coughing; if due to cold, use Ma Huang Tang; if due to heat, use Xie Bai San. If lung heat is in the chest, use Dong Yuan Liang Ge San; for thirst, use Ren Shen Bai Hu Tang; for sore throat, use Gan Ju Niu Bang Zi Tang; if there's a cough with phlegm, use Yu Ye Wan; if lung deficiency is severe, use Tiao Yuan Tang. The lung is the child of the spleen; if deficient, one should replenish its mother. Sometimes, simply use Sheng Mai San. Thus, the method is initially complete.

    If the lung has been ill for a long time, with persistent coughing, unceasing panting, or shoulder breathing, or if the chest is sunken, coughing up blood that does not stop, or coughing that causes fright, or if the nose is dry and blackened, or the nostrils are flaring and panting, or if there is persistent diarrhea, loud roaring like a barrel, or if the face appears emaciated with reverse panting—these are all signs of lung exhaustion; without treatment, they would worsen.

    Heaven is the true essence concentrated at the Gate of Life; without the celestial pulse, a person is rootless like a tree without roots.[20p]
    The essence of the kidneys should be strong, for water cannot withstand the burning of two fires. The kidneys belong to water, and they arise from the true essence of heaven. A person has kidneys just as a tree has roots. The pulse is checked at the wrist; the state of the kidneys can be observed through the wrist pulse. The life gate is situated between the kidneys, where the original qi gathers with sincerity. The strength or weakness, longevity or premature death of a child is especially connected to this. A complete mastery requires no deficiency.

    If the kidney qi is insufficient, it will sink down, as the heavy bones desire to drop and retract the body. Kidney water is of the yin; if the kidneys are deficient, the eyes fear light. The child is fundamentally weak and timid, stemming from a failure of the prenatal qi which leads to insufficient spirit. The whites of the eyes are abundant, and the skull becomes relaxed; the complexion appears pale and white, all of which are difficult to nourish. Sometimes, this could be due to illness rather than kidney deficiency; this belongs to the signs of illness.

    The kidneys govern the bones; if the kidneys are deficient, the marrow is not full. Children are particularly afraid of the cold, often suffering from maladies involving weakness. If the coccyx is undeveloped, they cannot sit; if the kneecaps are undeveloped, they cannot walk. Teeth are the surplus of bones; if bones are insufficient, teeth emerge slowly. The fluid of the kidneys is blood, and hair is the surplus of blood; if the kidneys are deficient, the hair is sparse and not black. The openings of the kidneys are in the ears; if the kidneys are deficient, the ears become thin, and heat may lead to the discharge of pus from within.

    The kidneys open to the two yin, and if the kidneys are hot, there will be obstruction in urination; if cold, urination will resemble rice water.[21p]
    The second fire refers to the fire of the ruler and minister. The classic states: "One water cannot withstand two fires." This is exactly the meaning. The yin is always insufficient, and the kidneys are often deficient; therefore, the tendons and bones cannot fully develop, leading to emaciation. The Qian clan's treatment mainly focuses on replenishment. The classic mentions that sores and rashes require purgation and the rest. Water represents yin, and fire represents yang; when one water cannot withstand two fires, it indicates excess yang and insufficient yin, clearly showing the deficiency at the root of the kidneys. Therefore, the Qian clan only uses the Replenishing Kidney Dihuang pill. They dare not purge, due to a lack of concrete evidence. Some claim that for rashes, the kidneys should not be nourished but instead purged. This statement is quite erroneous. The kidneys govern fluids; the blood transformed in rashes becomes water, and this water transforms into pus, all of which are derived from the kidney's fluids. If the kidney water is absent, the sores would dry up, turn black, and lead to death. How could one possibly purge? The sickness of rashes labeled as returning to the kidneys indicates that the poison of the sores and rashes arises from the marrow and manifests externally on the skin; when it turns black and sinks back into the marrow, it becomes harmful. This is not harm caused by the surface but a disease of excess fire and diminished water. The Qian clan treats blackened and sunken issues with Baixiang pills and Niuli paste to purge the evil within the kidneys, not the true yin of the kidneys. This is elaborated in "Essentials of Rashes." For kidney heat and constipation, it is advisable to guide it with pig bile.[22p]
    The pig is an aquatic animal. For those who have difficulty with urination, it is advisable to use Wuling Powder to drain the bladder. Dongyuan’s Ziyin Pill is used to dispel kidney fire. If kidney disease persists, leading to downward sinking of the body, and one perceives ghost-like images in the eyes, or experiences weakness in the bones, unable to rise from bed, or suffers from loss of bowel and bladder control, these are signs of kidney depletion and are difficult to treat.

    The discussion of the internal organs is based on the mental/spiritual aspect, distinguishing clear methods of supplementation and draining. If they are seen to share coexisting diseases, it is more appropriate to consider their interrelation and modify the approach accordingly.

    According to the "Nanjing", there are discussions about five evils: The genuine condition involves the internal organs themselves, while the external pathologies that come from the front are considered real; those that come from behind are seen as empty; evils that arise from being overpowered are termed subtle evils, and those that do not hold power over are referred to as thieves. This aligns with the theory of the five elements of generation and overcoming.

    Qian’s assessment states that the liver governs wind, the heart governs fright, the spleen governs obstruction, the lungs govern wheezing, and the kidneys govern emptiness. All of these pertain to primary internal diseases, termed genuine and evil, thus establishing methods of five supplements and six drains. Mr. Jiegu took the words of the Nanjing to elucidate the evidence of transformation in the five organs, supplementing aspects that Qian’s theory did not cover, ensuring a complete method. Hence, wind harms the liver, heat harms the heart, dampness harms the lungs, cold harms the kidneys, and exhaustion from food intake injures the spleen. These pertain to evils that afflict the five organs themselves, marking them as the primary illness.[23p]
    The liver is responsible for wind, and the wind in this context refers to the primary illness, known as true and false pathogens. If the condition is due to injury from heat, the true pathogen is the heart invading the liver; if it arises from injury by dampness, the false pathogen is the kidney invading the liver; if it results from dietary strain and fatigue, the minor pathogen is the spleen overcoming the liver. The other organs resemble this pattern. For detailed understanding, refer to the "Forty-Nine Difficulties."

    In the discussion of treatment methods for the five organs, if the liver is directly affected, the treatment should focus solely on the liver, using Qing Wan for drainage. If the heart is invading the liver, the appropriate remedy is to use Dao Chi to drain the heart, which effectively addresses the root issue. If the kidney injures the liver, one should use Jiang Fu Si Ni Tang to strengthen the kidney deficiency, thereby nourishing its mother. If the lung transmits to the liver, the recommended approach is to use Xie Bai San to drain the lung and Di Huang Wan to nourish the liver, first nourishing and then draining. If the spleen burdens the liver, it is advisable to use Tiao Yuan Tang to benefit the spleen and regulate the liver. The same reasoning applies to the other organs.

    For other methods, there is no need for rigid adherence; they can be understood and applied flexibly. These all address the initial onset of the illness.

    Moreover, when one organ's illness affects another, it is termed a "concurrent syndrome," and the treatment should consider the urgency of the primary and secondary conditions. The initially observed condition is termed the "root" and is treated as less urgent, while the subsequent condition is called the "branch" and is treated as more urgent.[24p]
    If there is difficulty in urination or defecation, persistent vomiting or diarrhea, swollen throat and pain, inability to eat, or urgent pain in the heart and abdomen, even if these symptoms appear later, they should be treated first. Therefore, it is said that in emergencies, one treats the symptoms. If there are no urgent symptoms, one should treat the initial illness first, and then address subsequent ailments based on their manifestations, which is known as treating the root when the situation allows.

    In general, a child’s spleen issues are often due to improper balancing of milk and food. Knowing that other organ problems require harmonizing the stomach is vital; otherwise, it can lead to malnutrition and suffering. The stomach governs the intake of grains, while the spleen is responsible for their digestion. Hunger can harm the stomach, and overfeeding can insult the spleen. Children often suffer from overeating. If a mother is robust and has abundant milk, seeking to prevent the child from crying can lead to excessive breastfeeding, which can damage the milk's properties. Conversely, if the mother is weak and thin, her milk will be scarce, and to soothe the child’s cries, she may resort to giving them grains, meats, pastries, and fruits, leading to overindulgence and harm from food.

    Thus, children's ailments are mostly related to the stomach. The five organs rely on the stomach's qi for nourishment. The stomach represents a balance of vital energy, unlike the individual weaknesses of the five organs. If any of the organs are affected, whether through purging or tonifying, one must be cautious not to disturb the stomach's qi. If the stomach's qi is damaged, it may lead to inability to eat and weight loss, or good appetite with weight loss, resulting in malnutrition which cannot be treated. As the classic says: “Whole grains lead to prosperity; absence of grains leads to demise." This is indeed a critical insight in the medical field.[25p]

    Five Zang Organs and Their Related Diseases

    These are diseases arising from the movement of qi within the five zang organs, indicating illnesses that originate internally. The liver governs wind; when abundant, it leads to straight vision, yawning, loud crying, and a feeling of tension and discomfort in the neck. When deficient, it causes teeth clenching and yawning. If qi is warm, it internally generates wind; if qi is hot, it generates external wind as well. Qi here refers to the breath in the mouth. In cases of excess, use Xieqing pills or Danggui Longhui pills to purge; in cases of deficiency, use Dihuang pills to tonify.

    All wind-related symptoms, convulsions, and distortions are indicative of liver disease and should be treated with Xieqing pills. Diseases originating from the liver, such as dizziness due to wind, belong to the wood element of the liver. The "Pulse Canon" states: heat generates wind. If there is a concurrent heart condition, it can result in fever and convulsions. If there is wind in the liver, it can cause the eyes to twitch lightly; if there is also heat in the heart, it can lead to blockage. If there is heat in the liver, the eyes may see straight without twitching; if heat in the heart is present, twitching occurs. Use Xieqing pills to purge the liver and Daochi powder to purge the heart.

    If there are also symptoms from the spleen, mild cases may result in drowsiness and lack of appetite; one should observe the state of the stool. If the stool is dry, use honey-based remedies to gently guide it out, being careful not to propose purgation, for fear it may lead to spleen deficiency and worsen the condition. If the stool is moist, use Hupo Baolong pills as the treatment.[26p]
    When there are also lung symptoms, with rapid breathing and a feeling of tightness, phlegm and mucous blockages must be resolved through urination and defecation. If the breathing sounds are audible, shoulders are raised, and the chest is high, with phlegm noises in the throat, it should not be treated. The Qingning Powder is prescribed.

    When there are also kidney symptoms, with sudden hoarseness and loss of voice, along with stiff limbs, this should be treated for wind. In mild cases, the Dihuang Pill is used; in severe cases, it becomes a chronic condition that cannot be treated.

    The heart governs shock; if it is real, there will be crying and fever, and a tendency to convulse after drinking water; if it is empty, there will be fatigue, insomnia, and restless palpitations. For real conditions, the Daohong Pian herbal decoction is prescribed; for empty conditions, the Er An Shen Pill is used.

    Various manifestations of heat, shock, and agitation with frequent crying indicate a primary heart condition. The Daohong Powder with朱砂 (cinnabar) is suitable for treatment. In severe cases, the Liangjing San Huang Xie Xin Wan should be used.

    Diseases arising from the heart, as the texts say: all pains, itching, sores, and ailments belong to heart fire.

    When there are also liver symptoms, there may be fever and convulsions, in which case the Mutong Powder should be administered.

    When there are also spleen symptoms, with excessive sleep, dreaming of grinding teeth, and frequent shock, the Qian Family An Shen Pill should be prescribed.

    When there are also lung symptoms, with fever, convulsions, and wheezing, the Qingning Powder should be administered.

    When there are also kidney symptoms, there may be sudden fainting, teeth grinding, convulsions, and cold hands and feet upon onset; after the episode, one wakes up in a daze. This is because the heart houses the spirit; shock harms the spirit; the kidneys store will; fear harms will.[27p]
    When a child is mentally timid and fearful, their spirit becomes unsettled and can lead to convulsions. As mentioned in the scriptures, when a monk is asked to recite mantras while touching the child's head, if the child becomes frightened, they may develop convulsions and later react when they see someone in dark clothing. Some may experience prolonged fear leading to convulsions; if treated early, they can be cured using the Ding Zhi Wan. If parents are negligent and do not treat it for long, it becomes a lifelong issue.

    The heart fire represents the sovereign fire, which ought to cultivate virtue and not be toxic; when it causes itchiness or sores, it is the result of the ming men fire. Any sores on children stem from fetal toxins.

    The spleen governs dampness, resulting in true fatigue or sleepiness, and a warm body prompting the need for water; if this leads to vomiting or diarrhea, it generates wind. If dampness is excessive, it can be treated with Xie Huang San or San Huang Wan; if it's deficient, it's treated with Yi Huang San, Yi Gong San, Xiao Jian Zhong Tang, or Tiao Yuan Tang, and Fei Er Wan for nourishment.

    Sleepiness without appetite, along with vomiting and diarrhea, are all root issues of the spleen. For heavy sleep and fever, Wei Ling Wan or Hu Po Bao Long Wan should be used. For vomiting and diarrhea, if cold, the person will not feel thirsty, and Li Zhong Wan is appropriate; if hot, they will crave cold water, with Wu Ling San or Tiao Tian Shui San advised.

    The diseases arising from the spleen, as stated in the classics, indicate that all dampness and swelling are related to the spleen's soil.[28p]
    When symptoms of the liver are present, initially caused by wind, with vomiting and diarrhea, accompanied by aversion to wind and fever, along with restlessness and anxiety, one should disperse these symptoms using the Xingsheng San. If vomiting and diarrhea occur first, followed by a transformation to slow and startled responses, it is untreatable.

    When symptoms of the heart are present, such as fever and drowsiness, with frightful dreams, one should use the Dongyuan Anshen Wan to treat it. If there is thirst and a desire to drink water, one should use the Chen Sha Wuling San.

    When symptoms of the lungs appear, with fever and drowsiness, and difficulty breathing accompanied by wheezing, one should use the Tingli Wan to address it.

    When symptoms of the kidneys are evident, such as emaciation and weakness, with a propensity to lie down and an inability to rise, one should supplement both the spleen and kidneys. To replenish the kidneys, one should use the Dihuang Wan; to replenish the spleen, the Yangpi Wan should be used. If diarrhea persists and results in bloody pus, it is fatal. The kidneys are the source of vital energy; if they are deficient, the constitution will be insufficient. The spleen is responsible for the production of qi; if it is weak, this leads to a deficiency of fluids. Therefore, among children’s diseases of the five organs, the spleen and kidneys are most affected, followed by the liver and heart, with the lungs being the least affected.

    The lungs govern wheezing; in cases of excess, there will be chaotic wheezing and difficulty breathing, accompanied by a desire for water, or even refusal to drink; in cases of deficiency, there may be constricted breathing and prolonged exhalation. In cases of excess, the Xie Bai San and Tingli Wan should be used to purge, while in cases of deficiency, Ejiao San and Sheng Mai San combined with Gan Ju Tang should be used to supplement.

    All wheezing and shortness of breath, coughing, and facial swelling, are fundamental diseases of the lungs and should be treated with the modified Xie Bai San.[29p]
    Two qian of balloon flower root and windbreak herb, one qian of licorice, and one qian and two fen of earth bone bark.

    Diseases of the lungs, according to the classics, say: all ascending qi and reverse breath belong to the lungs. If liver signs are also present, caused by wind stroke, with clear nasal discharge and aversion to wind along with cough and wheezing, it is advisable to disperse, using a modified Shen-Su decoction. If there is a chronic cough that transforms into a wind disease, it should not be treated. As referred to by the Qian family, three purges of the liver will not alleviate liver disease, and three tonifications of the lungs will still leave lung symptoms particularly deficient.

    If there are also heart symptoms, with fever, thirst, and chaotic breathing, this indicates excessive heart fire. It is advisable to use Cool Diaphragm Powder with added Zhimu and gypsum. For a persistent cough, a recipe of Huanglian and Ejiao pills is suitable. Huanglian and red Poria can suppress heart fire, leading to liver purification.

    If there are also spleen symptoms, causing cough and expectoration, this indicates damage from dairy and food, leading to unsettled cough. It is advisable to use Tingli pills or Little Xiantian pills with added Dahuang.

    If there are also kidney symptoms: the kidneys are the water organ, receiving and storing the fluids from the five organs and six bowels. Fluids enter the heart as sweat, the liver as tears, the lungs as nasal discharge, the spleen as saliva, and the kidneys as essence.[30p]
    Coughing with an abundance of phlegm indicates that the essence of the kidneys is not returning to the source. It is advisable to use the Rehmannia Six Formula as the main treatment, supplemented with ingredients like prepared Morinda root, stir-fried Eucommia bark, and liquor-washed Cistanche, along with stir-fried fennel and stir-fried Euphorbia herbs, ground into a powder and formed into honey pills, then taken with a decoction of Ophiopogon.

    The kidneys govern the void, not the solid. The Rehmannia formula addresses this. However, in cases of smallpox where the kidneys are solid, this notion is not articulated by the Qian family but is an error of the record-keeper, and it is unclear. To clarify doubts for future generations, there exist formulas to drain the kidneys, such as the Baixiang pill. There are also theories for tonifying the spleen and draining the kidneys, which may lead to children's misfortunes; thus, relying entirely on books is less beneficial than having none at all.

    The human body consists of the lungs governing the skin and hair, the heart governing blood vessels, the spleen governing muscles, the liver governing tendons, and the kidneys governing the marrow. The kidneys, among the five organs, are akin to winter among the four seasons. The poison of sores and rashes emerges from the marrow, affecting the muscles, blood vessels, and skin, similar to how seasonal goods accumulate in winter, then disperse to give rise to spring life, summer growth, and autumn storage.

    If it turns black and returns to the kidneys, it cannot disperse outward but instead retreats inward; this reflects a deficiency of true qi in the kidneys and an excess of pathogenic qi. Hence, formulas like the Baixiang pill and Niu Li syrup are established to dispel the pathogenic qi from within the kidneys, not to deplete the true qi. Moreover, the water in the kidneys nourishes and strengthens, filled with fluids.[31p]
    For black and sunken rashes, it indicates the kidneys are primarily deficient, where water cannot overcome fire, and fluids are dried up, leading to a blackened appearance that sinks inward. The treatment of such conditions is to drain excess fluids to save fire.

    All deficiencies and weaknesses, particularly in those with poor constitution from pregnancy, are diseases of the kidneys. After illness affecting the five organs occurs, if there is kidney deficiency, use Di Huang Wan with modifications according to symptoms. Rashes related to the kidneys may require both draining and tonifying.

    Regarding kidney-related illnesses, Qian's theory states: the kidneys are the source of deficiency, manifesting from insufficient prenatal endowment.

    If there are also liver symptoms, such as convulsions and limb paralysis, use Di Huang Wan with the addition of two liang each of Niu Xi, Dang Gui, and Xu Duan, and one liang of powdered cinnamon, making into honey pills for consumption.

    If heart symptoms present, with convulsions and loss of voice, use Di Huang Wan added with two liang each of Shi Chang Pu, Bai Zi Ren, and Yuan Zhi, grinding them into powder to create honey pills.

    For spleen symptoms, including vomiting, diarrhea, and dysentery, employ Di Huang Wan with two liang each of Huang Lian and Huang Bai stir-fried in wine, and one liang each of stir-fried Gan Jiang, Che Qian Zi, ground Nutmeg, making into a honey pill for ingestion.

    In cases with lung symptoms, where cough includes blood-stained phlegm, use Di Huang Wan with two liang each of Tian Men Dong, Mai Men Dong (roasted), Zhi Mu, Huang Bai prepared with honey water, and roasted Ejiao for honey pill preparation.[32p]
    According to the methods of supplementing and draining based on the strengths and weaknesses of the five organs, we interpret the classics. The classics say: when the evil qi is abundant, it is real; when the true qi is lost, it is deficient. The so-called "real" refers to the expelling of evil qi; the "deficient" refers to the replenishing of true qi. When true qi is robust, one is like a healthy child, how can there be a need to drain? If the liver is often in excess and the spleen often deficient, this indicates the inherent qi of the organs. The liver represents the lesser yang qi; at the birth of a child, like a tree budding, it embodies the growing energy of the lesser yang, gradually strengthening, hence its abundance. The intestines and stomach are delicate and thin, and the essence of grain is not yet sufficient, which accounts for the spleen's deficiency.

    When infants exhibit bright and clear colors and have a strong, resonant voice, this indicates sufficient heart and lung qi. When they are able to consume milk and food, with regulated bowel movements, this shows adequate qi in the intestines and stomach. When the hands and feet are warm, and the muscles and bones are strong, this indicates sufficient kidney and liver qi. This is known as being easy to care for when free from illness, and indiscriminate use of medicine is unwise.

    Conversely, if the complexion is pale and the voice is soft, this indicates insufficiency in heart and lung. If milk and food intake decreases and there are frequent vomiting and diarrhea, this shows insufficiency in the intestines and stomach. If the neck is soft, and the hands and feet are weak, this indicates insufficiency in liver and kidney. Such children are often ill and difficult to nurture. This distinguishes between the strengths and weaknesses of the five organs based on physical condition. For those who are ill, treatment should follow the specific strengths and weaknesses of the five organs.[33p]
    Treatment of Internal Organ Diseases

    The method of treatment is generally as follows: for liver diseases, the priority is to dispel wind and regulate qi; for heart diseases, the urgent approach is to suppress fire and tranquilize disturbances; for spleen diseases, it is necessary to warm the middle and resolve stagnation; for lung diseases, the focus is on descending qi and clearing phlegm; and for kidney diseases, the aim is to replenish true essence. This outlines the main principles of treatment.

    If lung disease also presents with liver symptoms, where one grinds their teeth and yawns frequently, it is easier to treat, as liver deficiency can’t support the lung. However, if one is crying out sharply with a stiff neck and irritability, treatment becomes difficult. This is because prolonged lung disease leads to deficiency and coldness, while a strong liver can overpower the lung. Treatment should consider the freshness, duration, deficiency, and excess of the illness: for deficiency, nourish the mother; for excess, drain the child.

    The liver, being primarily affected by wind, leads to yawning and irritability, along with heat in the mouth, which should be dispersed using Daqinggucao. If appetite is present and water intake is excessive, a small dose of Dahuangwan should be given, without excess purging. If there’s liver heat causing one to fidget with their clothing or twist objects, Xieqingwan is appropriate. For strong fever, excessive drinking, and wheezing, Bai San should be administered. When liver diseases overshadow the lung, particularly in autumn, where a strong liver prevails over a weak lung, it is necessary to tonify the spleen to treat the liver. Strengthening the spleen enables the mother to fortify the child. Use Bu spleen Yihuang San to treat liver with Xieqingwan.[34p]
    When the liver has wind, the eyes blink excessively without spasming; if heat arises from the heart, then spasms occur. The treatment is with Qing Wan for liver excess and Dao Chi San for heart issues. When the liver has heat, the eyes direct their gaze without spasming; the same treatment applies. When the liver is affected by wind, the body becomes stiff and straight, not spasming, and warmth does not affect the heart; in such cases, one should tonify the kidneys to treat the liver. The main treatment is with Di Huang Wan for kidney tonification and Qing Wan for liver excess. Regardless of whether the illness is new or chronic, it all stems from the movement of liver wind, which directs its action towards the head and eyes. The eyes pertain to the liver; when wind enters the eyes, they flutter lightly as if blown by wind, making it difficult for the child to remain still, hence the excessive blinking. If heat enters the eyes, it pulls on their tendons and both corners become tense, making it impossible to turn the gaze, hence the fixed stare. If accompanied by heart heat, spasms occur because both the mother (heart) and child (liver) possess real heat, leading to the clash of wind and fire.

    In autumn, liver conditions are observed as the wood element strengthens the liver, overpowering the lungs. Therefore, it is advisable to tonify the lungs and drain the liver. In mild cases, liver issues alleviate; in severe cases, there may be pallor of the lips and death.

    When there is heart heat, sleep is affected, and the breath feels warm within the mouth. Sometimes, there is a tendency to sleep with the face covered, and there may be grinding of teeth at night—all indicative of heart heat, for which Dao Chi San is the main treatment. When heart qi is heated, the chest also feels warm, creating an urge to speak but resulting in a desire to remain still as if feeling cold, hence the tendency to sleep face down. If heart qi is full, it creates a blockage of qi movement, and sleeping in a compact position hinders flow, thus one prefers to sleep on one’s back to allow for unobstructed upward and downward movement of qi; accordingly, Xie Xin San is the main treatment.[35p]
    Heart disease appears in winter; when fire is strong and the heart overcomes the kidney, one must tonify the kidney and treat the heart. In mild cases, the disease retreats; in severe cases, there is a descent without speech, indicating a weak and deficient kidney.

    When the spleen and stomach are not harmonious, the face appears pale and lacks vitality, the breath is cold, there is no appetite, and one vomits water; one must tonify the spleen, using Yihuang San as the main treatment. If the spleen and stomach are deficient and cold, the face is pale, thin, and weak, with abdominal pain and loss of appetite; one must tonify the spleen, using Yihuang San. For diarrhea, use Tiaozhong Wan; if there is a cold from wind, with cold limbs, the spleen is weak; one must harmonize the spleen, then disperse the cold. Harmonizing the spleen with Yihuang San, disperse using Daqing Wan as the main treatment. For spleen diseases, address all nearby conditions in this manner. Those with a favorable disposition are easier to treat, while those with an unfavorable disposition are harder to treat. Weakness of the spleen may present with a reddened yellow face; treat the corresponding organ according to the symptoms.

    If there is excess lung condition along with cold wind, with fullness in the chest, shortness of breath, gasping, and wheezing, one must first disperse the lung and then release the cold wind. To disperse the lung, use Xiebai San as the main treatment. If the lung is only injured by cold, there will not be fullness in the chest; if there is heat in the lung, the hands may press against the eyebrows, eyes, nose, and face, treated with Ganjiao Tang. For lung deficiency with heat, resulting in deep red lips, treat by dispersing lung deficiency heat with a smaller dose of Xiebai San. If the lung is weak and the lips are pale, one must tonify the lung, using Ejiao San as the main treatment.[36p]
    If one experiences agitation, coarse breathing, and wheezing, it is difficult to treat due to lung deficiency. Chronic spleen and lung disease leads to deficiency, resulting in pale lips. The spleen is the mother of the lungs; when both are deficient, they cannot nourish each other, hence the term "timid." The lungs correspond to the lips; if the lips are pale and lustrous, it is a good sign, but if they are white like dry bones, it foretells death. Lung diseases that appear in spring indicate that the lungs overpower the liver; thus, one should tonify the kidneys and liver and treat the lungs. If the liver is weak, it leads to illness. To tonify the liver and kidneys, use Di Huang Wan; for treating the lungs, use Xie Bai San. In spring, if lung ailments arise and the lungs are robust, one should purge the lungs. In mild cases, the lung disease will recede; in severe cases, pale blue eyes may indicate fright. Additionally, if redness appears, it suggests a weak liver, which is also indicated by pale blue eyes.

    A child with kidney deficiency is originally weak and timid, due to insufficient prenatal energy resulting in insufficient vital essence. Such children have often white sclera, a reflective forehead, a wide face, and a pale complexion, all of which are difficult to nurture, typically living only up to 88 days. If one indulges excessively in desires, they may not survive beyond 40 days. Some may develop kidney deficiency due to illness, which is not part of this discourse. Furthermore, insufficient kidney energy leads to sinking; certainly, heavy bones desire to drop down and hunch the body. The kidneys represent yin; thus, kidney deficiency causes light sensitivity, so one should tonify the kidneys with Di Huang Wan. When kidney ailments present in summer, water overcomes fire; the kidneys overpower the heart, and one should purge the kidneys. In mild cases, the illness may recede; in severe cases, palpitations may occur as well.[37p]
    On the Liver

    Qian Zhongyang states: The liver governs wind. When it is full, there will be loud shouting and urgency in the neck, causing annoyance. When it is deficient, one may grind their teeth and yawn. If there is heat in the Qi, wind arises externally; if the Qi is warm, wind arises internally, to be treated with Daqing Gao. If one can continue to eat and drink without interruption, use Dahuang Wan to gently purge. If the liver is hot, the eyes will bulge without twitching, and the hands will fidget with clothing or twist items. Use Xieqing Wan to treat this. If there is strong heat, resulting in thirst and shortness of breath, Xie Bai San should be administered.

    Liver ailments appear in autumn; if the lung is weak and cannot support the liver, benefit the spleen with Yihuang San, and Xieqing Wan should be used to treat the liver. If there is wind in the liver, the eyes will blink rapidly. If heart heat causes twitching, use Xieqing Wan for the liver, and Daohong San for the heart. In severe cases, the body may arch back, the eyes bulge without twitching, the heart is not affected by heat; use Dihuang Wan to nourish the kidneys, and Xieqing Wan to treat the liver. Those with pale lips should not be treated.

    Furthermore, Zhang Jiegu states: The liver governs wind; if ill, it will cause wind to convulse and tense. If heart is strong in the liver, it is a pathogenic evil; if the lung seizes the liver, it is a thief evil; if the kidney regulates the liver, it is a deficiency evil. In all cases of liver illness, one must first examine the lungs and kidneys. The kidney is the mother of the liver; the lung is the thief of the liver.

    Hence, if the liver is ill, and it is not due to the kidney water's inability to generate it, it is likely due to the lung's metal demon harming it. Therefore, if the cause is in the lungs, first treat the lungs and attack the demon; if the cause is in the kidneys, first nourish the kidneys to replenish the source. Then, assess the condition of the primary organ for emptiness or fullness and for cold or warmth. I secretly believe that if there are symptoms of excess heat in the liver channel leading to external wind, it is suitable to use Daqing Gao for treatment.[38p]
    If after taking the medicine the symptoms still worsen, it indicates that the evil qi has left but the spleen qi is deficient. In this case, it is advisable to use Yigong San with additional Xiangfu and Angelica for replenishment. If there is liver channel deficiency heat, or internal wind generated from oppression and constriction, Yigong San and Di Huang Wan should be used for nourishment. If wind evil has entered the organs and causes cold food intake and constipation, this indicates internal excess of evil qi; thus, it is appropriate to use Dahuang Wan to purge it. If after purging there is a reduced appetite and an abdominal distension, this indicates internal deficiency of spleen qi; hence, Baizhu San should be used for replenishment.

    If one has naturally weak qi and blood, possibly due to a post-illness condition, or from taking purgatives, and they often seek their collar, grind their teeth, yawn, and have pale eyes, this points to severe liver channel deficiency; therefore, Di Huang Wan should be urgently used to nourish the kidney and liver. If there are symptoms of choking breath, shortness of breath, and prolonged exhalation, this indicates severe lung channel deficiency; Yigong San should be urgently utilized to nourish spleen and lung.

    If one cries out during the Shen (3-5 PM) and You (5-7 PM) hours, stares blankly, yawns irritably, feels anxious, and has shaky hands and feet, with a fever and thirst, this is due to the clash of wind and fire overpowering lung metal. Chaihu Zhi Zi San should be used to treat liver fire and promote liver blood; Yigong San should nourish spleen earth and promote lung metal.

    If the lips appear pale, this indicates extreme spleen deficiency and is untreatable. For infants, symptoms often arise from the mother's indulgent diet, inappropriate breastfeeding, or due to the nurse’s diet causing agitation. Once the disease qi has manifested and the physical form is deficient, one should ascertain the cause and administrate herbs including Lu Lu to treat the mother while the child takes one or two spoonfuls. Afterward, continue in this manner.[39p]
    The Heart

    Qian Zhongyang said: The heart governs fright; when it is strong, it manifests as crying, fever, drinking water, and convulsions; when it is weak, it leads to fatigue, restlessness, and palpitations. He also stated: When there is heat, the breath during sleep is warm, and one may grind their teeth or sleep with their face up, showing a tendency to cool down, which indicates heart heat; this is treated with Daohong San. If one sleeps on their back, it indicates strong heart qi, and the qi cannot circulate up and down; this requires Xiexin San for treatment. Heart issues manifest in winter, showing that fire overcomes water; one should nourish the kidneys to treat the heart, and mild cases may resolve on their own. If there is downward descent and silence, it indicates kidney deficiency and timidity. Furthermore, Zhang Jieguh stated: The heart governs heat; if the lungs invade the heart, it creates a slight pathogenic influence; if the liver invades the heart, it results in a deficiency; if the spleen invades the heart, it results in a real pathogenic influence; if the kidneys invade the heart, it leads to a thieving influence. Whenever the heart becomes ill, it is essential to first adjust the liver and kidneys. When liver qi flows smoothly, heart qi becomes harmonious; when liver qi is stagnant, heart qi becomes weak. Thus, for heart issues, one must first seek to address the liver and clear the source.[40p]
    When the five organs suffer illness, the disease will inevitably transmit to the organ it overcomes. The evil affecting the kidneys must transmit to the heart, hence one should first treat the kidneys to dispel the evil. Only when the liver and kidney channels are harmonized can one then assess the true and false conditions of the heart for treatment. I modestly believe that those who sleep on their backs do so because their chest is full of heat, thus they prefer to lie back and seek the empty space. Those who prefer to lie face down do so because their chest is deficient and hot, hence they prefer to lie prone to seek fullness. If it’s a case of fullness, one should adjust and treat the heart and liver; if it’s a case of deficiency, one should tonify the spleen and lungs. These two conditions should be distinguished clearly. Symptoms, such as teeth grinding, may share similarities and do not require rigid adherence to specifics. If one uses formulas like Xie Xin and Dao Chi, although the evil qi is dispelled, the illness persists; one must then tonify the vital qi. If the situation worsens, one must urgently warm and tonify the vital qi. If heart qi appears in winter, or if at the time of the Pig or Rat hours the illness worsens, or if there is a reluctance to speak, this indicates deficiency of kidney water and excess of heart fire; one should use Di Huang Wan. For infants under mother’s care, it is necessary for the mother to take it.[41p]
    Spleen

    Qian Zhongyang states: The spleen governs the condition of being troubled; actually, it refers to trouble in sleep and body heat, whether drinking water or not. In cases of distress, vomiting and diarrhea arise from wind. If the spleen and stomach are deficient and cold, the face appears pale and weak, the eyes lack brightness, the breath from the mouth and nose is cold, the body is thin and weak, there is vomiting, abdominal pain, and a lack of desire for food; benefit can be gained from the Use of Huang San; for bowel movements, use the Tiao Zhong Wan. If there are cold hands and feet due to a wind affliction, it indicates a weakness of the spleen. First use Huang San to replenish the spleen, then use Da Qing Gao to disperse it. Spleen diseases manifest similarly across the four seasons. Those in harmony are easier to treat, while those against the flow are hard to treat. A weak spleen may present with a red or yellow face; if it also interacts with the five organs, treat according to the symptoms. Moreover, Zhang Jiegu states: The spleen governs dampness; when sick, there is often diarrhea and excessive sleep, with a heavy and lethargic body. If the liver invades the spleen, it is a thief's evil; if the heart invades the spleen, it is a void's evil; if the lung invades the spleen, it is a real evil; if the kidney invades the spleen, it is a minor evil. In all spleen diseases, one must first investigate the liver and heart organs. Indeed, the liver is the ghost of the spleen, and the heart is the mother of the spleen.[42p]
    When liver qi is excessive, ghostly evils persist; when heart qi is deficient, vitality is insufficient. One should harmonize liver qi and nourish heart qi. If the pulse indicates that both liver and heart are harmonious, then the spleen is affected, and one should assess the deficiency and excess to treat it. I suspect that in cases of actual evidence, the pathogenic qi is excessive while the vital qi is deficient. If the complexion is pallid, with vomiting, diarrhea, and abdominal pain, and the breath is cold from the mouth and nose, this pertains to cold water invading earth, and one should use Yi Huang San. If the complexion is bluish and lips dark, with vomiting, diarrhea, and cold in the hands and feet, this indicates spleen deficiency with cold, and one should use Gan Jiang Li Zhong Tang. If the complexion is sallow-yellow, and the hands and feet are not cold, this indicates a weak spleen, and one should use Ren Shen Li Zhong Tang. If there is a wind condition with cold in the hands and feet, expectoration, coughing, and diarrhea with abdominal distension, this indicates a deficiency in both spleen and lung qi, and one should use Wu Wei Yi Gong San to strengthen spleen qi, adding Fang Feng and Sheng Ma to expel external evils. If it arises during the time of Yin and Mao, one should use Liu Jun Zi, Chai Hu, and Sheng Ma to nourish spleen earth and pacify liver wood. However, a yellow complexion is the natural color of the spleen. A red complexion indicates fire generating earth, which is harmonious; a bluish complexion indicates wood conquering earth, which is disharmonious. One should harmonize what overcomes to replenish the original qi effectively.[43p]
