    I surmise that conditions of downward sinking whereby the feet dislike being covered indicate that everything below the waist is governed by the kidneys, as the heart qi descends to the kidney region. The method is to use Rehmannia Six Formula to strengthen kidney water and control heart fire. If kidney water cannot be generated due to weakness of the spleen and lungs, one should use the Si Jun Zi Decoction and Rehmannia Six Formula to nourish the source of transformation. For sores and rashes that are dark and depressed, it indicates kidney deficiency with excess harmful qi, thus especially indicating the use of Rehmannia Six Formula.[47p]

    　　　　古今医鉴 【明　龚信】

    　　　　　五脏生成

    　　夫一月之孕，有白露之称；二月之胚，有桃花之譬。及其三月，则先生右肾而为男，阴包阳也；先生左肾则为女，阳包阴也。其次肾生脾，脾生肝，肝生肺，肺生心，以生其胜己者。肾属水，故五脏由是为阴。其次心生小肠，小肠生大肠，大肠生胆，胆生胃，胃生膀胱，膀胱生三焦，以生其己胜者。小肠属火，故六腑由是为阳。其次三焦生八脉，八脉生十二经，十二经生十二络，十二络生一百八十丝络，丝络生一百八十缠络，缠络生三万四千孙络，孙络生三百六十五骨节，骨节生三百六十五大穴，大穴生八万四千毛窍，则耳目口鼻四肢百骸之身皆备矣。[48p]

    "The Medical Mirror of Past and Present" by Gong Xin (Ming Dynasty)

    The Generation of the Five Organs

    In the first month of pregnancy, it is referred to as "white dew"; in the second month, it is likened to "peach blossom." When it reaches the third month, the right kidney produces a male, as the yin wraps around the yang; the left kidney produces a female, as the yang wraps around the yin. Then the kidneys give rise to the spleen, the spleen gives rise to the liver, the liver gives rise to the lungs, and the lungs give rise to the heart, thus generating those that overcome themselves. The kidneys belong to water, so the five organs are therefore yin.

    Following this, the heart gives rise to the small intestine, the small intestine gives rise to the large intestine, the large intestine gives rise to the gallbladder, the gallbladder gives rise to the stomach, the stomach gives rise to the bladder, and the bladder gives rise to the three energizers, generating those that overcome their own nature. The small intestine belongs to fire, hence the six fu organs are therefore yang.

    Next, the three energizers give rise to the eight vessels, the eight vessels give rise to the twelve meridians, the twelve meridians give rise to the twelve collaterals, the twelve collaterals give rise to one hundred eighty fine collaterals, the fine collaterals give rise to one hundred eighty entwined collaterals, the entwined collaterals give rise to thirty-four thousand sub-collaterals, the sub-collaterals give rise to three hundred sixty-five joints, the joints give rise to three hundred sixty-five major acupoints, and the major acupoints give rise to eighty-four thousand pores. Hence, all the ears, eyes, mouth, nose, limbs, and body are complete.[48p]

    　　　　　观面部五脏形色歌

    　　心经有冷目无光，
    　　太阴黑，目无光彩，此心经冷也。
    　　面赤须言热病当。
    　　面颊赤色，此为心有热也。
    　　赤在山根惊四足，
    　　山根赤色，心经生风，下至准头恶也。　　积看虚肿起阴阳。
    　　三阴三阳虚肿，心有积也。
    　　肝经有冷面微青，
    　　面青为肝受冷，主发惊也。[49p]

    Observing the Shape and Color of the Five Organs on the Face

    The Heart Channel is cold, with eyes lacking brightness,
    The Taiyin is dark, with eyes without luster; this indicates the coldness of the Heart.
    A flushed face suggests heat diseases to address.
    Red cheeks signal that the Heart has heat.
    Red at the root of the nose indicates agitation in the limbs;
    Red at the root of the nose suggests wind in the Heart Channel, leading to misfortune in the forehead.
    Accumulated observation reveals swelling of yin and yang.
    Three yin and three yang swell; this indicates accumulation in the Heart.
    The Liver Channel shows coldness with a slight bluish tinge on the face,
    A bluish face indicates cold affecting the Liver, which is associated with startling reactions.[49p]

    　　有热眉泡赤又临。
    　　眉上有红赤，为肝有热也。
    　　发际白言惊气入，
    　　发际至印堂略白者，为肝惊也。
    　　食仓黄是积热深。
    　　眉上有红赤，为肝有热也。
    　　脾冷应知面色黄，
    　　面黄印堂反白者，为脾冷也。
    　　三阳有白热为殃。
    　　三阳上白者，为脾热也。
    　　青居发际生惊候，
    　　发际及印堂色青者，脾惊也。
    　　唇口皆黄是积伤。
    　　上下唇黄，为脾受积也。
    　　肺受面白冷为由，
    　　白色在面皮，及人中或青者，皆肺冷也。　　热赤人中及嘴头。
    　　人中及嘴头有赤者，肺有热也。
    　　青在山根惊四足，
    　　山根青色，是肺受惊也。
    　　赤居发际积为仇。
    　　发际赤色，乃有积也。
    　　面黑当知肾脏寒。
    　　面带黑者，肾有冷也。
    　　食仓红是热须看。
    　　食仓红者，肾有热也。
    　　风门黄可言惊入，
    　　风门黄者，肾有惊也。
    　　两目微沉积所干。[50p]

    There is heat indicated by red on the eyebrows.
    Red above the eyebrows means the liver has heat.
    White at the hairline suggests a shock has entered the energy.
    If the hairline and the area between the eyebrows are slightly white, it indicates liver shock.
    Yellow in the food storage area indicates deep accumulation of heat.
    Red on the eyebrows means the liver has heat.
    If the spleen is cold, the complexion will be yellow.
    If the face is yellow and the area between the eyebrows is white, it indicates spleen cold.
    White heat in the three Yangs leads to disaster.
    If white appears above the three Yangs, it indicates spleen heat.
    If blue appears at the hairline, it indicates shock.
    If the hairline and the area between the eyebrows are blue, it indicates spleen shock.
    Yellow lips indicate accumulated damage.
    Yellow on both the upper and lower lips indicates spleen accumulation.
    White cold on the face signifies issues with the lungs.
    If whiteness appears on the facial skin or under the nose, or if it is blue, it indicates lung cold.
    Red in the area under the nose and on the lips indicates lung heat.
    Blue in the root of the nose signifies shock affecting the limbs.
    Blue at the root of the nose indicates lung shock.
    Red at the hairline signifies accumulation of issues.
    Red at the hairline indicates accumulation.
    A black face suggests kidney cold.
    A blackened face signifies cold in the kidneys.
    Red in the food storage area indicates heat to be observed.
    Red in the food storage area indicates kidney heat.
    Yellow at the wind gate suggests a shock has entered.
    Yellow at the wind gate indicates kidney shock.
    The eyes appear slightly sunken due to accumulated issues.[50p]

    　　两目微沉，是积在肾也。

    　　　　医学纲目 【明　楼英】

    　　　　　五脏

    　　五脏相胜，病随时令，乃钱氏扩充《内经》藏气法时论之旨，实发前人所未发者也。假如肝病见于春及早晨，乃肝自病于本位也。今反见于秋及日晡肺之位，如肺虚极，肝往胜之，故当补脾肺泻肝也。余仿此。　　洁古曰：热则从心，寒则从肾，嗽而气上从肺，风从肝，泻从脾。假令泻兼嗽，又气上，乃脾肺病也，宜泻白、益黄散合而服之。脾苦湿，肺苦燥。气上逆也，其证见泻，又兼面色黄，肠鸣呦呦者，宜服理中汤。泻而呕者，宜服茯苓半夏汤。如泻而渴热多者，宜服黄芩厚朴汤。不渴而热少者，宜服白朮厚朴汤。其他五脏若有兼证，皆如此类推之。更详后论四时推详用药。　　心主热，自病或大热，泻心汤主之。实则烦热，黄连泻心汤主之。虚则惊悸，生犀散主之。　　肺乘心，微邪，喘而壮热，泻白散主之。肝乘心，虚邪，风热，煎大羌活汤下大青丸主之。[51p]

    The two eyes are slightly sunken, which indicates accumulation in the kidneys.

    Medical Guidelines (Ming Dynasty, by Lou Ying)

    The Five Organs

    The interdependence of the five organs leads to illnesses corresponding with seasonal changes. This reflects the expanded interpretations of the "Inner Canon" on the method of conserving Qi, a concept previously unexplored. For instance, if liver disease manifests in spring or early morning, it indicates an inherent issue with the liver. If it later presents in autumn or late afternoon, corresponding to the lungs, and if the lungs are extremely deficient, the liver may prevail, thus requiring remedies for the spleen and lungs while draining the liver. I follow this principle accordingly.

    The ancient texts state: Heat originates from the heart, cold from the kidneys, coughing rises from the lungs, wind from the liver, and diarrhea from the spleen. If diarrhea is accompanied by coughing and rising Qi, it indicates a spleen-lung condition, hence one should use a combination of Baihua and Yihuang powders. The spleen suffers from dampness, while the lungs suffer from dryness. If the Qi is reversed up and symptoms show diarrhea with a yellow complexion and rumbling intestines, one should take Lizhong Decoction. For those with diarrhea and vomiting, Fuling Banxia Decoction is advisable. If there is diarrhea with significant thirst and heat, Huangqin and Houpian Decoction is suitable. For those not thirsty but with less heat, Baizhu and Houpian Decoction should be used. Other combinations of the five organs should be extrapolated similarly. Further discussions will elaborate on seasonal approaches for medication.

    The heart governs heat; if there is inherent or significant heat, Xiexin Decoction is prescribed. If it is excessive heat, Huanglian Xiexin Decoction is appropriate. In cases of deficiency leading to fright or palpitations, Shengxi San is used.

    The lungs are influenced by the heart, presenting mild pathological factors such as wheezing with strong heat, in which case Xiebai Powder is utilized. The liver affects the heart with weak pathogenic factors, presenting with wind-heat; Da Qianghuo Decoction combined with Daqingwan is warranted.[51p]

    脾乘心，实邪，泄泻身热，泻黄散主之。肾乘心，贼邪，恐怖恶寒，安神丸主之。　　肺主燥，自病则喘嗽，燥则润之。实则喘而气盛，泻白散主之。　　虚则喘而少气，先益黄散，后阿胶散主之。　　心乘肺，贼邪，热而喘嗽，先地黄丸，中导赤散，后阿胶散主之。肝乘肺，微邪，恶风眩冒昏愦嗽，羌活膏主之。肾乘肺，实邪，憎寒嗽清利，百部丸主之。脾乘肺，虚邪，体重吐痰泄泻嗽，人参白朮散主之。　　肝主风，自病则风搐拘急。肝苦急，急食甘以缓之，佐以酸苦，以辛散之。实则风搐力大，泻青丸主之。虚则风搐力小，地黄丸主之。　　心乘肝，实邪，壮热而搐，利惊丸凉惊丸主之。肺乘肝，贼邪，气盛则前伸呵欠微搐，法当泻肺，先补本脏。补肝，地黄丸主之；泻肺，泻白散主之。脾乘肝，微邪，多睡体重而搐，先当定搐，泻青丸主之；搐止再见后证，则别立法治之。肾乘肝，虚邪，憎寒呵欠而搐，羌活膏主之。[52p]

    The spleen dominates the heart; when it becomes excessive, it causes heat in the body, and the Yellow Scattering Powder is used to alleviate this. The kidneys affect the heart; if they bring an evil qi, it may lead to fear and aversion to cold, treated with the Anshen Pill. The lungs govern dryness; if ill, it results in coughing and wheezing; thus, dryness should be moistened. If excessive, it leads to wheezing with strong qi, treated with the White Scattering Powder. If deficient, there is wheezing with little qi, first use the Yellow Scattering Powder, followed by the Ejiao Powder.

    The heart influences the lungs; if there is an evil qi, it brings heat and wheezing, managed first with the Dihuang Pill, then the Red Scattering Powder, followed by the Ejiao Powder. The liver affects the lungs; if slightly in disarray, it may cause aversion to wind, dizziness, and coughing, treated with the Qiang Huo Ointment. The kidneys impact the lungs; if excessive, they provoke aversion to cold and clear cough, managed with the Baibu Pill. The spleen influences the lungs; if deficient, it leads to heaviness, phlegm, diarrhea, and coughing, treated with the Ginseng and Atractylodes Powder.

    The liver governs wind; if ill, it results in convulsions or spasms. If the liver is in distress, consuming sweet foods helps to alleviate it, combined with sour and bitter to disperse. If excessive, it produces strong convulsions, treated with the Qing Pill. If deficient, it results in weaker convulsions, managed with the Dihuang Pill.

    The heart affects the liver; if in excess, it brings vigorous heat and convulsions, treated with the Lijing Pill and Liangjing Pill. The lungs impact the liver; if evil qi is present and qi is strong, it results in yawning and slight convulsions; lung drainage is necessary, starting with tonifying the organ. For reinforcing the liver, the Dihuang Pill is used; for draining the lungs, the White Scattering Powder is needed. The spleen influences the liver; if slightly affected, it leads to excessive sleep and heaviness, and convulsions must first be stabilized, treated with the Qing Pill. If convulsions stop and other symptoms reappear, then a separate method should be established for treatment. The kidneys affect the liver; if deficient, they bring aversion to cold and yawning with convulsions, treated with the Qiang Huo Ointment.[52p]

    　　脾主湿，自病则泄泻多睡，体重昏倦。脾苦湿，急食苦以燥之。实则泄泻赤黄，睡不露睛，泻黄散主之。虚则泄泻色白，睡露睛，白朮散主之。　　肝乘脾，贼邪，风泻而呕，茯苓半夏汤主之。心乘脾，虚邪，壮热体重而泻，羌活黄芩苍朮甘草汤主之。肺乘脾，实邪，能食不大便而呕吐嗽，煎槟榔大黄汤下葶苈丸。肾乘脾，微邪，恶寒泄泻，理中丸之类主之。　　肾主寒，自病则足胫寒而逆。人之五脏惟肾无实，小儿疮疹变黑陷，则是肾实水克退心火。　　心乘肾，微邪，内热不恶寒，桂枝汤主之。肺乘肾，虚邪，喘嗽皮濇寒，百部丸主之。肝乘肾，实邪，拘急气搐身寒，理中丸主之。脾乘肾，贼邪，体重泄泻身寒，理中丸主之。　　凡五脏虚弱，是自己正令不行，乃鬼贼之所克害，当补本脏之正气。假令肺病喘嗽时，于初春见之，法当补肾。见于夏救肺，见于秋泻肺，见于冬补心泻本脏，又名寒泻。[53p]

    The spleen governs dampness; when it is ill, there is often diarrhea, excessive sleep, and a feeling of heaviness and fatigue. The spleen suffers from dampness, so bitter foods should be consumed to dry it out. In cases of excessive dampness, diarrhea appears red and yellow, with closed eyes while sleeping; for this, Ban Xia and Huang Qi Decoction is used. In cases of deficiency, diarrhea is pale, with eyes open during sleep; for this, Bai Zhu Decoction is used.

    The liver influences the spleen, causing evildoers, wind, diarrhea, and vomiting; for this, Fu Ling and Ban Xia Decoction is used. The heart affects the spleen, resulting in deficiency and heat, with heaviness and diarrhea; for this, Qiang Huo, Huang Qin, Cang Zhu, and Gan Cao Decoction is used. The lung influences the spleen, causing excessive conditions where food is consumed but leads to no bowel movements, and vomiting and coughing occur; for this, a decoction of areca nut and rhubarb is used, along with Ding Li pills. The kidney affects the spleen, causing mild evildoers, coldness, and diarrhea; for this, formulas like Li Zhong Wan are used.

    The kidneys govern coldness; when they are ill, the legs and shins feel cold and inverted. Among the five organs, only the kidneys do not have an excess. If a child’s rash turns black and sinks, this indicates that the kidneys have excess water, countering heart fire.

    The heart influences the kidneys, causing mild evildoers, internal heat without aversion to cold; for this, Gui Zhi Decoction is used. The lung affects the kidneys, leading to deficiency, wheezing, coughing with cold; for this, Bai Bu pills are used. The liver influences the kidneys, causing excess conditions with tightness and cold; for this, Li Zhong Wan is used. The spleen affects the kidneys, causing evildoers, heaviness, diarrhea, and cold; for this, Li Zhong Wan is also used.

    In cases where the five organs are weak, it signifies that the proper regulation is not functioning, thus being harmed by external evildoers. It is important to replenish the upright qi of the original organ. For instance, if there is lung disease with wheezing and coughing appearing in early spring, one should tonify the kidneys. In summer, address the lung; in autumn, involve the lung with diarrhea; and in winter, tonify the heart while addressing the original organ, also known as cold diarrhea.[53p]

    大抵五脏各至本位，即气盛不可更补，到所克位不可更泻。　　洁古曰：肝病面白，肺病面赤，脾病面青，肾病面黄，心病面黑。若肝病惊搐，而又加面白痰涎喘急之类，此皆难治。余仿此推之。假令春分前，风寒也，宜用地黄、羌活、防风或地黄丸及泻青相间服之。春分后，风热也，宜用羌活、防风、黄芩或泻青丸、导赤散下之。立夏后，热也，宜用三黄丸、导赤散。夏至后，湿热也，宜用导赤散、泻黄散合而服之；或黄芩、人参、木香之类。秋分后用泻白散，立冬后用地黄丸主之，谓不受泻也。　　海藏曰：补肝丸：四物汤内加防风、羌活等分为细末，炼蜜丸是也。　　镇肝丸：泻青丸，去栀子、大黄，治肝虚。　　泻肾丸：治脉洪而实，即前地黄丸，熟地改生地，去山茱萸是也。　　此治左手本部脉。若右尺洪实，以凤髓丹泻之。此地黄丸即仲景八味丸去桂、附。若加五味子，肾气丸也。此益肺之源，以生肾水焉。[54p]

    In general, when the five organs reach their natural states, the qi is abundant and cannot be further supplemented, while those that are subdued cannot be further drained. According to Jie Gu, liver disease manifests as a pale face, lung disease as a red face, spleen disease as a bluish face, kidney disease as a yellow face, and heart disease as a dark face. If liver disease presents with sudden shocks or convulsions, along with a pale face and symptoms like phlegm, saliva, and shortness of breath, these are difficult to treat. I infer similar cases from this.

    For instance, before the spring equinox, when the wind is cold, one should use Rehmannia, Qianghuo, and Fengfeng, or take Rehmannia pills and alternate with Qingxia decoction. After the spring equinox, when the wind is warm, one should use Qianghuo, Fengfeng, and Huangqin, or take Qingxia pills and Daohong powder. After the summer begins, when it's hot, one should use Sanhuang pills and Daohong powder. After the summer solstice, when it's humid and hot, one should take a combination of Daohong powder and Xiehuang powder, or similar herbs like Huangqin, Ginseng, and Muxiang. After the autumn equinox, use Xiebai powder, and after the arrival of winter, use Rehmannia pills as a primary treatment, which is not subject to drainage.

    Haicang states that for Liver Nourishment Pills: within the Siwu Decoction, add Fengfeng and Qianghuo in equal parts, ground into a fine powder, and then formed into honey pills. For the Liver Calming Pills: Xieqing pills, excluding Gardenia and Rhubarb, are used to treat liver deficiency. For the Kidney Draining Pills: they target a full and strong pulse, namely the aforementioned Rehmannia pills, substituting freshly prepared Rehmannia instead of the cooked version, and excluding Corni fruits. This treats the pulse of the left wrist. If the right wrist pulse is strong and full, use Fengsui Dan to drain it. The Rehmannia pills mentioned are the same as the Eight Flavor Pills by Zhang Zhongjing, minus cinnamon and aconite. If added with Schisandra, it becomes the Kidney Qi Pills, which nourish the lung's source and generate kidney water.[54p]

    　　　　古今医统 【明　徐春甫】

    　　　　　五窍相通应证

    　　心窍通于舌。心为脏，小肠为腑。心色赤，主夏三月。心味苦，心液汗，心主血，心声言，心气呵。有余笑，不足忧。《千金》云：心气实则笑不休，虚则悲不已。　　肝窍通两目。肝为脏，胆为腑。其色青，旺春三月。肝味酸，肝液泪，肝主筋，肝声泣，肝气嘘。有余怒，不足悲。《千金》云：怒则实，悲则虚。　　脾窍通唇口。脾为脏，胃为腑。其色黄，旺四季月。脾味甘，脾液涎，脾主肌肉，脾声歌，脾气呼。有余腹满，不足少气。　　肺窍通鼻孔。肺为脏，大肠为腑。其色白，旺秋三月。肺味辛，肺液涕，内主气，外主皮毛，肺声哭，肺气呬。有余喘，不足叹息。　　肾窍通两耳。肾为脏，膀胱为腑。其色黑，旺冬三月。肾味咸，肾液唾，肾主骨，肾声呻，肾气欠。有余泄泻，不足则厥逆。[55p]

    Medical Connections Between the Organs

    The heart is connected to the tongue. The heart is an organ, and the small intestine is a cavity. Its color is red and it is dominant during the three months of summer. The heart tastes bitter, its fluid is sweat, it governs blood, its voice is speech, and its energy is breath. When in excess, it leads to laughter; when deficient, it results in worry. According to "Qianjin," when the heart’s energy is full, one laughs incessantly; when it is empty, one weeps continuously.

    The liver is connected to the eyes. The liver is an organ, and the gallbladder is a cavity. Its color is green, and it is dominant during the three months of spring. The liver tastes sour, its fluid is tears, it governs the tendons, its voice is weeping, and its energy is exhaled breath. When in excess, it leads to anger; when deficient, it results in sadness. According to "Qianjin," anger is fullness, while sadness is emptiness.

    The spleen is connected to the lips and mouth. The spleen is an organ, and the stomach is a cavity. Its color is yellow, and it is dominant during the four seasonal months. The spleen tastes sweet, its fluid is saliva, it governs the muscles, its voice is singing, and its energy is breath. When in excess, it leads to a feeling of fullness in the abdomen; when deficient, there is a lack of energy.

    The lungs are connected to the nostrils. The lungs are an organ, and the large intestine is a cavity. Its color is white, and it is dominant during the three months of autumn. The lungs taste spicy, their fluid is mucus, they govern energy internally and the skin externally, their voice is weeping, and their energy is gasping. When in excess, it leads to wheezing; when deficient, it results in sighing.

    The kidneys are connected to the ears. The kidneys are an organ, and the bladder is a cavity. Its color is black, and it is dominant during the three months of winter. The kidneys taste salty, their fluid is saliva, they govern the bones, their voice is groaning, and their energy is weakness. When in excess, it leads to diarrhea; when deficient, it results in cold extremities.[55p]

    　　　　　五脏克绝

    　　心病目黑，肾克心，壬癸日绝。肝病皮黑，肺克肝，庚辛日绝，脾病唇青，肝克脾，甲乙日绝。肺病颊肿目赤，心克肺，丙丁日绝。肾病面肿唇黄，脾克肾，戊己日绝。
    　　　　证治准绳 【明　王肯堂】

    　　　　　五脏

    　　张洁古曰：五脏子母虚实，鬼贼微正，若不达旨意，不易得而入焉。在前者为实邪。子能今母实，拒贼伤于母，其子又引母所克者妻，来相助，故曰实邪也。在后者为虚邪。母引子之鬼贼至，由母能使子虚也。《内经》云：子能令母实，母能令子虚，此之谓也。妻来乘夫为微邪，夫来乘妻为贼邪，法当泻鬼补本脏。本脏自病为正邪，当虚则补之，实则泻之。经云：滋苗者必固其根，伐下者必枯其上。逆其根，伐其本，则败其真矣。[56p]

    The Five Organs and Their Pathologies

    When the heart is ill, the eyes become dark; the kidney injures the heart, leading to extreme deficiency of the water element (ren and gui). When the liver is ill, the skin becomes dark; the lung injures the liver, causing a deficiency of the metal element (geng and xin). When the spleen is ill, the lips turn cyan; the liver injures the spleen, resulting in deficiency of the wood element (jia and yi). When the lung is ill, the cheeks swell and the eyes turn red; the heart injures the lung, causing deficiency of the fire element (bing and ding). When the kidney is ill, the face swells and the lips turn yellow; the spleen injures the kidney, resulting in deficiency of the earth element (wu and ji).

    Principles of Diagnosis and Treatment

    Zhang Jiegugu stated: The five organs have a relationship of mother and child between deficiency and excess; the ghosts and thieves are subtle or apparent. If the intent is not reached, it becomes difficult to enter. The excess pathologies are in the front; the child can now cause the mother to be excessive, repelling the thieves that harm the mother. The child also calls for assistance from what the mother restrains, hence termed as excess pathology. The deficient pathologies are in the back; the mother brings the child’s ghost and thief, as the mother can cause the child to be deficient too.

    The Inner Canon states: The child can cause the mother to be excessive, and the mother can cause the child to be deficient. This is what it's referring to. When the wife comes to dominate the husband, that’s termed a subtle pathology; when the husband comes to dominate the wife, that’s termed a thieving pathology. The treatment should focus on dispelling the ghosts and nourishing the root organ. When the root organ itself is ill, this is the proper and improper pathology. If it’s deficient, then nourish it; if it’s excessive, then drain it. The classic states: To nourish the sprouts, one must secure the roots; to cut from the bottom, one must dry out the top. To reverse the roots and cut at the base will ruin the true essence.[56p]

    　　肝胜肺则肝病，身热发搐，又见肺虚。喘而气短，病见于申酉戌时，是肝真强也。经云：受所制而不能制，谓之真强。法当补脾肺而泻肝，导赤散、泻黄散主之。　　刘宗厚云：此皆五脏相胜，病机不离五行生克制化之理者，盖小儿初生襁褓，未有七情六欲，只是形体脆弱，血气未定，脏腑精神未完，所以有脏气虚实胜乘之病。但世俗不审此理，往往遇是率指为外感内伤而用药，致枉死者多矣。悲夫！钱氏论时有脱略，幸而洁古补之。今特参附，诚无穷之惠也。
    　　　　　五脏补泻法

    　　钱氏曰：凡病先虚，或已经下，有合下者，必实其母，后泻其子也。假令肺虚而痰实，此可下之证，先当益脾，后方泻肺也。　　泻青丸又名泻肝丸。[57p]

    If the liver prevails over the lungs, it leads to liver disease, with body heat causing convulsions, and signs of lung deficiency appear. When one experiences wheezing and shortness of breath, and the illness manifests during the hours of Shen, You, or Xu, this indicates a strong liver. The classics say: to be constrained and yet unable to control is termed true strength. The appropriate treatment is to tonify the spleen and lungs while draining the liver, using Daohong San and Xie Huang San as primary remedies.

    Liu Zonghou pointed out that all of this relates to the five organs overcoming each other, with the pathological mechanisms closely tied to the principles of generation and overcoming in the five elements. Infants, upon first entering the swaddling, have not yet developed the seven emotions and six desires; they are merely physically fragile, with unsettled blood and qi, and their organ spirits are incomplete, leading to conditions of deficient and excessive organ energy. However, common practice often overlooks this principle, frequently attributing such cases to external pathogens or internal injuries and thus leading to many wrongful deaths. How tragic! The writings of the Qian family sometimes miss key points, yet fortunately, Jie Gu has supplemented them. Now, I have specifically added these discussions, which are truly of boundless benefit.

    Methods of Supplementing and Draining the Five Organs

    Qian said: Whenever there is an initial deficiency, or it has already descended, one must first treat the mother organ before draining the child organ. For example, if the lungs are deficient but phlegm is excessive, this is an indication for purging; one should first benefit the spleen and then proceed to drain the lungs. The Xie Qing Wan is also known as Xie Gan Wan.[57p]

    　　钱氏谓肝无补法，故无补肝药。王海藏以四物汤加防风、羌活等分为细末炼蜜丸，名补肝丸。　　又以泻青丸去栀子、大黄，名镇肝丸，治肝虚。　　导赤散泻丙小肠。
    　　泻心汤泻丁心。
    　　安神丸治心虚疳热，神思恍惚。
    　　海藏八物定志丸，补心正药。
    　　益黄散，又名补脾散。海藏云：此剂补脾以燥湿。东垣云：治胃中寒湿，呕吐腹痛，泻利清白之圣药也。　　泻黄散，又名泻脾散。海藏云泻脾热。　　阿胶散，又名补肺散。海藏云杏仁本泻肺，非若人参、天门冬、麦门冬之类也。　　泻白散，又名泻肺散。海藏云治肺热骨蒸自汗，用此直泻之。栀子、黄芩亦泻肺，当以气血分之。　　地黄丸即金匮八味丸去桂、附。海藏云：治肾虚解颅，即鬾病也，治脉毛而虚。　　钱氏谓肾无泻法，故无泻肾药。海藏泻肾丸，治脉洪而实，即前地黄丸，熟地改生地，去山茱萸是也。此治左手本部脉。若右尺洪实，以凤髓丹泻之。[58p]

    Qian states that there are no methods to nourish the liver, thus there are no liver-nourishing medicines. Wang Haizang made a refined honey pill from the Siwu Decoction, adding Fangfeng and Qianghuo, naming it the Liver Nourishing Pill. He also created the Zhen Gan Pill by removing Zhizi and Dahuang from the Xieqing Pill to treat liver deficiency. Daohong San disperses heat in the small intestine.

    Xiexin Decoction drains the heart.

    Anshen Wan treats heart deficiency with symptoms of heat, causing the spirit to be confused and disoriented.

    Haizang's Babushisan stabilizes the mind and is a proper heart tonic.

    Yihuang San, also known as Bupi San, is said by Haizang to tonify the spleen and dry dampness. Dongyuan notes it treats cold dampness in the stomach, nausea, abdominal pain, and is a holy medicine for diarrhea with clear discharge.

    Xiehuang San, also known as Xiepisan, is noted by Haizang to drain heat from the spleen.

    Ejiao San, also called Bulei San, as stated by Haizang, treats the lungs. Xingren primarily drains the lungs, unlike ginseng, Asparagus adscendens, or Ophiopogon japonicus.

    Xie Bai San, also named Xie Fei San, according to Haizang, addresses lung heat with symptoms of bone steaming and spontaneous sweating, directly draining this condition. Zhizi and Huangqin also drain the lungs, differentiating between qi and blood.

    Dihuang Wan is simply the Jinkui Eight Ingredients Pill without Gui and Fu. Haizang claims it treats kidney deficiency leading to headaches, particularly for sallow symptoms and the pulse being weak.

    Qian argues that there are no draining methods for the kidneys, hence no kidney-draining medicines. Haizang's Xie Shen Wan treats a full and robust pulse, similar to the prior Dihuang Wan, substituting Shudihuang for Shengdihuang and omitting Sanjue. This addresses the primary pulse of the left hand. If the right pulse is full and strong, treat it with Fengsui Dan.[58p]

    　　　　医学入门 【明　李梴】

    　　　　　五脏形证

    　　肝风目直手循捻。
    　　 【注　气热为外伤风，气温为内生风，热则两眦俱紧不转。凡目直兼青者，必发惊；咬牙甚者，亦发惊。肝主谋，故循衣领，乱捻物。风甚身强反张力大，泻青。心乘，风火相搏则发搐，导赤散。渴喘，泻白散。】　　虚则咬牙呵欠兼。[59p]

    Introduction to Medicine
    (Ming - Li Chen)

    Symptoms of the Five Organs

    Liver wind: eyes fixed, hands circling and twisting.
    [Note: Qi heat is an external injury of wind, while Qi warmness is wind produced internally. When there is heat, both canthi tighten and do not move. If the eyes are fixed and have a bluish hue, it will surely cause fright; severe teeth grinding also induces fright. The liver governs planning, which is why one circles around the collar and randomly twists objects. If the wind is strong, the body becomes resilient and tense, resulting in blue discharge. The heart is affected when wind and fire clash, causing convulsions and red dispersions. Thirst and wheezing produce white dispersions.] If there is deficiency, then there will be teeth grinding and yawning.[59p]

    　　 【注　心不受热，目连札不搐，或发搐力小，俱当补肾治肝，肾气丸。如心乘肝等兼证，详见《纲目》。所谓乘者，犹乘车之乘。五脏相乘莫测，如肝病必先治肺补肾，然后审肝脏虚实而调之。余脏仿此。】　　心惊难言合面卧。
    　　 【注　心惊，搐也。烦热上窜，舌强欲言不能，叫哭。胸热，故欲合卧就凉。宜泻心汤、导赤散、小生犀散。】　　虚则困卧惊悸添。
    　　 【注　温惊丸主之。】
    　　脾困身热渴不食。
    　　 【注　脾困，倦也。实则困睡不露睛，身热，渴欲饮水，或闭或泄黄赤色，宜泻黄散。】　　虚则吐泻风生痰。
    　　 【注　虚则吐腥，泄泻白色，多睡露睛，四肢渐次生风，或有痰，钱氏白朮散、异功散、理中丸。如肝乘脾，风泄而呕，二陈汤加黄芩。】　　肺燥鼻干手掐目。[60p]

    "Notes: When the heart does not receive heat, and there is twitching without convulsion, or the convulsion is mild, both should be treated by supplementing the kidney and treating the liver with Kidney Qi Pills. If the heart rides on the liver along with other symptoms, refer to the 'Essentials' for more details. The term 'ride' is like riding in a vehicle. The interactions among the five organs are unpredictable; for instance, liver disease must first treat the lungs and supplement the kidneys, and then examine the liver for deficiencies or excesses to adjust accordingly. The other organs follow this principle."

    "Heart shock is hard to express, leading to a desire to lie down."
    "Notes: Heart shock causes twitching. Frustration and heat rise, leading to a strong tongue wishing to speak but unable to, causing crying. Chest heat results in a desire to lie down to cool off. Suitable remedies include Heart-Drain Decoction, Guide Red Powder, and Small Fresh Rhinoceros Powder."

    "In deficiency, it leads to fatigue and increased anxiety."
    "Notes: Use Warm Shock Pill as the main remedy."

    "Spleen fatigue leads to body heat, thirst, and loss of appetite."
    "Notes: Spleen fatigue refers to exhaustion. When excessive, it causes fatigue and sleep without opening the eyes, body heat, thirst for water, and possible yellow or red urine either in retention or leakage. The remedy should be Yellow Drain Powder."

    "In deficiency, it causes vomiting and diarrhea, yielding phlegm from wind."
    "Notes: In deficiency, there is regurgitation of a foul taste, diarrhea that is white, excessive sleeping with eyes open, and gradual onset of wind in the limbs and possibly phlegm; suitable remedies include Qian's White Atractylodes Powder, Different Effects Powder, and Regulating Middle Pill. If the liver acts on the spleen, leading to wind and vomiting, add Huangqin to Erchen Decoction."

    "Lungs dry, leading to a dry nose and pinching in the eyes."[60p]

    　　 【注　肺燥则喘嗽，宜则喘而气盛或渴，泻白散润之。手掐眉目具面者，甘桔汤主之。肺只伤寒则不胸满，胸热复有风冷，胸满短气喘嗽，泻白散、大青膏主之。】　　虚则少气喘无厌。
    　　 【注　虚则唇白色，气哽长出少气，先服益黄散，而后阿胶散。】　　肾寒畏明颅自解。
    　　 【注　肾只不足，小儿肾虚皆难养多夭，有因病而致虚者可补。】　　下窜足热火欲炎。
    　　 【注　下窜者骨重，惟欲坠下而缩身也。足热不喜衣覆，心火下于肾部，宜肾气丸或正气汤。又肺病重见肝虚证易治，见肝热证难治。盖肺病久则虚冷，肝强实而反胜也。经曰：受所制而不能制，谓之真强。法当补脾肺而后泻肝。肺胜者，当补肝泻肺。然嗽久虚羸，不可服泻白散，宜肾气丸。五脏病机，不离五行生克制化之理，所以有脏腑虚实乘胜之病。世俗不审此理，往往率指为外感内伤，而用药枉死。此钱氏、洁古之功大矣哉！】[61p]

    **Notes: If the lungs are dry, it leads to wheezing and coughing; one should consider the symptoms of wheezing with a strong breath or thirst and use the Xie Bai San to moisten. If there is pressure in the chest due to lung cold without fullness, but a combination of heat and wind cold causing chest fullness, shortness of breath, and coughing, use Xie Bai San or Da Qing Gao.

    If there is deficiency, there will be slight breathlessness without satisfaction.

    Notes: If there is deficiency, the lips will appear pale, and the breath may be obstructed, leading to long, shallow breathing; first take Yi Huang San, then Er Jiao San.

    If the kidneys are cold, there is a fear of bright light.

    Notes: If the kidneys are insufficient, children with kidney deficiency are often hard to nurture and may have a high risk of early death; those who become deficient due to illness can be replenished.

    If there is downward sinking accompanied by heat in the feet desiring to ascend.

    Notes: If sinking occurs, the bones feel heavy, leading to a desire to bend down. Hot feet dislike coverings, and heart fire descends to the kidneys, so root a Kidney Qi Pill or Zheng Qi Decoction. Moreover, if lung disease is heavy and follows with liver deficiency, it is easier to treat; if with liver heat, it is harder to treat. This is because prolonged lung disease leads to cold deficiency, while strong liver energy can dominate.

    The classics say: to be controlled and yet unable to control is called true strength. Thus, the method should be to nourish the spleen and lungs first, then drain the liver. When the lungs are dominant, it is necessary to nourish the liver and drain the lungs. However, in cases of chronic cough and deficiency, Xie Bai San should not be taken; the Kidney Qi Pill is more appropriate.

    The diseases of the five organs do not escape the principles of the five elements of generation and overcoming, leading to imbalances of deficiency and excess in the organs. The common perception does not analyze these principles, often hastily attributing them to external pathogens or internal injuries, leading to ineffective treatments and unnecessary deaths. The contributions of Qian and Jie Gu are indeed substantial!**[61p]

    　　　　五脏绝歌 【明　乔岳】

    　　　　　心

    　　吐泻变为痢，血黑渴难当。
    　　心主血，心绝则血色变黑，虚燥而发渴。　　肌瘦难行坐，虚舌不缩藏。
    　　心主舌，绝则不能收。
    　　两脸如脂赤，
    　　痢久则面当无色，今面色反如脂者，心绝则阳虚上发也。　　无语口生疮。
    　　心主舌，绝则不能语。
    　　若向夏中得、更莫细思量。

    　　　　　肝

    　　眼目时时濇，浑身似醉人。频频只要睡，心烦又多嗔。　　肝绝则不能开视，故濇而只要睡。又肝主筋，力絶则如醉人，不能举也。又肝主怒，绝则多怒不止也。　　唇白眼泡肿，狂躁足啼声。东方应此候，病则不宜春。
    　　　　　脾

    　　面色黄时好，不可见相传。体弱憎寒甚，虫行觅食飡。　　脾主肢，体绝则体弱。又脾绝则肾逆乘之，故发憎寒。脾绝则胃热，故虫不安而上吐出。　　吃乳唇无力，齿露盖时难。[62p]

    The Song of the Five Organs
    By Qiao Yue, Ming Dynasty

    Heart

    Diarrhea turns to dysentery, black blood makes one difficult to endure thirst.
    The heart governs blood; when the heart is exhausted, blood color turns black, leading to emptiness and dryness causing thirst.
    Muscles weaken, making it hard to walk or sit, and the tongue becomes feeble, unable to retract or hide.
    The heart governs the tongue; when it is exhausted, it cannot retract.
    The face is red like grease;
    When dysentery persists, the face should lack color, yet now the complexion is like grease: the heart's exhaustion leads to yang deficiency causing outbreaks.
    No speech, the mouth develops sores.
    The heart governs the tongue; when exhausted, speech is impossible.
    If one suffers this in midsummer, further contemplation is unwise.

    Liver

    The eyes weep constantly, the whole body feels like a drunken person.
    Repeatedly craving sleep, the heart is troubled and irritable.
    When the liver is exhausted, vision cannot be clear, hence constant weeping and a desire to sleep.
    Additionally, the liver governs the tendons; when weakened, one feels like a drunk, unable to lift oneself.
    Also, the liver governs anger; when exhausted, one experiences continuous irritability and rage.
    Pale lips, swollen eyes, frantic and loud cries.
    In the east, there are signs of this condition; illness is unfit for spring.

    Spleen

    The complexion is yellow at times, but must not be relayed to others.
    The body is weak, highly intolerant of cold, and worms seek food and sustenance.
    The spleen governs the limbs; when it is exhausted, the body weakens.
    Moreover, when the spleen is exhausted, the kidney's energy rises against it, resulting in a dislike of cold.
    Absence of appetite leads to heat in the stomach, causing worms to unrest and regurgitate.
    Eating is feeble; lips lack strength, and exposed teeth are difficult to cover at times.[62p]

    　　脾主唇，绝则不能收掩其齿，又不能吮乳。　　眼倾休下药，
    　　眼眶属脾，绝则倾陷。
    　　免更住人间。

    　　　　　肺

    　　肺候应白色，莫使见绝形。鼻青孔燥黑，腹胀眼眶倾。　　肺主鼻，绝则肝逆乘之而色青。又肺绝则无涕，故孔黑燥也。肺主眼泡，绝则陷之。　　项直喘气急，胸凸没回声。
    　　肺主气，绝则喘急项直以引气也。气绝则胸中满凸，但有出气而无回气也。　　秋间逢此侯，四方别托生。

    　　　　　肾

    　　冷汗时时有，尿多夜里惊。
    　　肾绝则阴阳相离，故冷汗出而小便不禁。精者神之舍，绝则精神离，故夜里多惊。肾属阴，夜亦属阴故也。　　遍身生粟疥，手足冷如冰。
    　　阳尽不能充暖故也。
    　　项倒头难举，面黑没精神。
    　　肾绝则天柱骨倒，面目皆黑，无精神也。　　此候应壬癸，冬得殒其身。

    [63p]

    The spleen governs the lips; if it fails, one cannot close them over the teeth, nor can one suckle. The eyes are directed downwards; the eye sockets belong to the spleen; if they fail, they sink. One cannot remain in the human world.

    The lungs correspond with the color white; do not let them show signs of failure. If the nose turns bluish and the eye sockets are dark and dry, the abdomen is distended. The lungs govern the nose; if they fail, the liver will reverse and cause a bluish color. Furthermore, if the lungs fail, there will be no mucus, hence the dark and dry nostrils. The lungs also govern the eyelids; if they fail, they will sink. A straight neck with rapid breathing indicates that the lungs govern breath; if they fail, breathing becomes urgent and the neck straightens in an attempt to draw in air. When breath is exhausted, the chest will feel full and distended, producing outgoing breath without a return. In autumn, encountering this condition, one’s four directions will be estranged.

    In the kidneys, there is cold sweat at all times, frequent night urination, causing shock. When the kidneys fail, yin and yang become separated, hence the cold sweat appears and urination cannot be controlled. Essence is where the spirit resides; if it fails, the spirit departs, causing frequent shock at night. The kidneys are associated with yin, and night also belongs to yin. The whole body breaks out in grain-like sores; the hands and feet feel as cold as ice. This is because yang cannot warm the body. The head tilts and is difficult to lift; the face is dark and lacks spirit. When the kidneys fail, the heavenly pillar and bones collapse, the face becomes dark and devoid of spirit. This condition corresponds with the elements of ren and gui; in winter, one may perish.[63p]
